O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear son, I have completed this book which is the last of the science of medicine together with its fulfillment, and I have made an end through its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And in a vision it came to me that I would complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of the hands, namely 'surgery'.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of the hands is neglected in our region and is unfamiliar to all, it has been lost, and nothing remains of the ancient knowledge except for small descriptions in books that have been handled by hand.Et quanque li fuers ne puet estre prescheve par les livres ne par les uers, et n’est riens quere demore, si convient que le corps soit traittre en la cirurgie, et li fuers estorbes par les mains, s’il poait estre.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, closed intentions, and alienated knowledge.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	Now it seems to me that I want to enliven it together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation;
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and I will come together with the forms of the instruments of cautery, and other tools of the work with the adjustment of their declaration and preparation as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And one who undertakes this must surpass in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, as far as he knows the judgment of members, and forms and conjunctions and separations of veins, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and sinews and the number of teeth, and the movement and of their veins both moving and resting, and from where they originate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And for this reason Hypocras says that the name with the name is much, and with the work is little;
et meismement en l’art de main.	and especially in the art of surgery.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you at the beginning of this book that anyone who is not familiar with the things mentioned above, be careful that he does not make a mistake and harm people;
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	so that I have many times encountered several of those who intervene in this science and abandon it without knowledge or experience.Et qui conisse la science, il doit la garder et la conserver;
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish man who cupped an abscess of scrofula on a woman's neck, and cupped the arteries in her neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	so much blood issued forth that the woman died between his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I saw another man who treated a stone in a man's groin; the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	he carried away with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I saw another who lanced a vein in the breast of a woman and gave her all the blood that was in the vein, so that the woman died then. And I had already been called to treat her, and I saw the nature of the disease and the size of the stone, and if they cut it out she would have died then.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another fool who treated the Duke of our land, who had a broken leg, and with the break there was a wound;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the foolish doctor bound the break above the wound with strong ligatures, and did not leave any wadding at the wound, and left it like that;
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and he commanded that he must not remove it;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and it remained thus, the leg swollen and the foot, until it came to ruin.And I saw another fool who treated an abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, and cupped the arteries in her neck;
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and loosen his leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I had loosened it, he was at ease and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	However, the corruption in the limb was already confirmed, and I could not heal it;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and the corruption did not cease from going through the limb until the member was completely destroyed.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another doctor who lanced an abscess that had become infected due to the negligence of his lord.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	Because a ulcer, when it is pure of melancholy humor, one should not touch it with iron unless it is in such a place that one can completely remove all that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And so, dear son, you should know that the work of medicine is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is, there is danger in many conditions;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show in each chapter of this book where there is doubt and fear.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	And so it is necessary that you be careful, so that foolish people do not speak badly about you.Car maintes fois il arrive que leu li corps est en tel cas qui n’est pas a leur pouvoir de le guérir, si que il
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you take up your arms in battle, and embark on your campaigns lightly and resolutely, and follow the best course so that by the grace of God you attain victory and are praised;
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave behind the terrible diseases of the body;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and lay aside your arms so that you may be delivered from what makes you hesitate, and have faith in yourselves so that you may pass from this world to the next with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galen says in one of his warnings:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not neglect a serious illness, lest you be called a foolish doctor."Si l’om medecine ne peut la guérir, querrez la divine provence qui nule chose ne laisse de ce
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have arranged this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapter is about fire cauteries and medical cauteries, and it is an ordered chapter from the head to the feet.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	It includes the forms of instruments, and the application of cauteries, and all that is necessary for the procedure.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and about cupping, and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things.
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	And this chapter includes instructions and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about resetting dislocations and twists, and similar things.
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	And it includes instructions for the head down to the feet, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus, as we remember the work, it is fitting that I describe the nature of aid and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the quality of aid, and the cause of harm, are the most lengthy subjects and subtle sciences, and the secret remedies;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	And about this, many wise men have spoken and agreed upon it;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	And I am content with their words, for I desire brevity.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cautery aids universally in all conditions, provided there is matter present, except in two conditions;
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	that is to say, hot condition without matter, and dry condition without matter.Car si li cauteres trove la matere, li cauteres li destroeit li matere et li mal, por ce ke
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a complex hot and dry nature together with matter, some people have devised and said that cautery is of great help.
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and others say the contrary:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that cautery does not benefit illness that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	Because the nature of fire is hot, it should not be treated with heat or dryness in a hot disease; and in a cold and moist nature, cautery is an aid.
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and those who say the contrary argue that cautery helps greatly with hot and dry diseases that originate in the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	Because when you compare the human body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this opinion.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found this to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And nevertheless, one should not undertake it if he has not experienced it, and who knows through long usage the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of men's complexions, and their dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and their outcomes and the season.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	We have no fear of other complexions, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians agreed and concurred about the use of cauteries.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my son, that a cautery combines fire with the secrets of healing, and is of greater benefit than a burning cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	Because fire is simple, and does not harm except the member which is burned, and does no harm to any other part if properly applied.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	Burning medicines pass from one limb to another by moving away, and bring great sickness to the limbs through poor healing.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and sometimes they kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, because of its height and the goodness of its substance, does not do this if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And I have discovered this through experimentation and through the length of service and study that I have devoted to the craft; and I have considered the truth of things;
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and because of this I will excuse myself from the length of my speech, for I do not wish to take away the secret that is reserved for fire, and the quality of its work, describing how it cures the illnesses of the body, as the philosopher explains in his demonstration.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	Now receive this into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on which days cauteries should be performed, and chose a suitable time.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is suitable at all times because the harmful humors are drawn out by the help of cautery;
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and likewise if the cautery is for painful and urgent conditions that cannot wait until a more serious evil afflicts the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think, dear son, as fools do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the disease that is healed by cautery does not return;
et il le dient ensi;	and thus they hold it:
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not as they believe, for cauteries are not what they think, since cautery is a medicine that moves the complexions, dries up the humors that cause pain, and is superior to other medicines due to its swiftness, its virtue, and its lordly power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is possible that the disease may sometimes come according to the complexions of the patient, the site of the disease, and its power;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and the excesses are gathered in him through the digestion of foods and similar things, unless cautery is administered to dry up the excess moisture in the place where there is little superfluity and moisture, as with tooth cauteries for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return;
mais ce avient poc.	but this rarely happens.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cauterization is called the last resort of medicine, and that is because:
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	they believe that cauterization should only be used after other medical treatments have failed, but their understanding is flawed. Cauterization is the last resort of medicine because when we have tried various treatment methods for a disease and they don't work, then we turn to cauterization, and it does work.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is clear that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish people.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancient scholars said that cauterization with a gold instrument is gentler than with iron, and they said so because of the quality of gold and the highness of its substance.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	They also said that the heat of the cautery does not cause blisters, but this is not true, as I have experimented and found it to be true in some people:
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and cauterization with gold is better than with iron, just as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And yet when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it cools down immediately;
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if it is heated too much;
si font au feu;	if they are made in the fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and so there is enough difficulty.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this we use fire cautery, which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have arranged this chapter from the head to the feet so that the way is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is useful for moisture and coldness on the head, and there are two reasons for it being used in a disease called "soda", and because of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, and ears, and for many diseases that come from coldness such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged with a cleansing, purgative medicine for 3 or 4 days, depending on what the strength, age, and condition of the patient can bear;
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then make the head of the cautery.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands and place his hands on top of his knees;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	afterwards, place the palm of your hand between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and let it come to your two middle fingers, and then bleed from there and heat the cautery which is called "olive", of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And place it over the spot marked with ink, and while lowering and drawing your hand back and forth, gently twist it;
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	then slowly raise your hand, and return to the spot if you see a little hole in the bone;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you don't see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	afterwards, take a bit of salt and place it in soft cotton, put it over the spot, and leave it for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	afterwards, put dampened cotton on top;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and let it stay until the blister is gone;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards, treat the wound with the ointment called 'tetrafarmaçon' until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the elders say that the more a wound stays open, the more it drains;
et por ce si aide mues.	and for this reason, movement helps.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some say that one must leave the cautery in place until part of the bone is burnt, and then have the burnt portion of bone removed and the wound healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And the others say that one must let the cautery burn so high, and press so hard that they lower the bone as widely as a woman's thimble, so that the humors can flow out.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one must leave the wound open for a long time;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	afterwards, one must clean and sutured it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem good to me in any way, except in some people where there is fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and I think that I should let it be;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	because the head is weakened by continued dissolutions of nature, as we testify in other members;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and likewise, when the shoulder of the sick person is weakened by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is milder for me, and with this I work together for salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of headache
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When chronic headache comes and lasts a long time, the patient should use herbs and pills called "cochie", and purgatives for the head, and oils and plasters.
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	And if they perform the cautery we mentioned before and it doesn't work,
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take care that the head of the patient is not of a cold nature, and is not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	then cauterize him under that cautery a little bit as we said above. Et s’il ne wert pas amendoin, et se li cauteres par les oiles qui qu’il ait, et
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	And if it is not better and the cauteries with the oils he has do not help, then cauterize each horn of the head to the bone, as we said before, and cauterize in the place called "vessel". et s’il ne wert pas amendoin, si fai li cautere sus l’esgouttoir dou chief, qui est apelez «vasselz», si com nous avons dit desus.
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and are used to treat wounds.
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and lighten your hand so that you do not touch the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patient feels much more pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and the cauteries for horns should be more delicate than those used to cauterize the middle of the head, and this is how it is done:
dou cautere dou chief	of the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When sudden pain arises in the head and the disease extends to the eye, and the shoulder is purged with cleansing medicines, and all other remedies I have described in the section on diseases have been tried without success:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	then you must perform cauterization in two ways, that is, with hot iron and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	For the cauterization with hot iron, take a small piece of alder wood, remove the bark and apply it to the shoulder in such a way that you can place the wood under the skin;
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it is bound, tie it well and leave it thus for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	then untie it and apply a poultice of garlic, leaving the wound like that for two or three days;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then put on linen soaked in butter until pus comes out.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the wound has healed, treat it with ointment until it is completely healed;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you see any of the burning medicines I have written about in the twelfth treatment of burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done in this way.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery until it is hot enough to use.
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called 'close' because the head is formed in the shape of a lid or has a small protuberance, and in the middle there is a small appearance;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and place it on the painful area, and hold your hand and gently turn the fire a little bit so that half of the thickness of the skin is burned;
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and hold your hand over the artery until it stops pulsating and flows with an abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	After this, put cotton in the wound and apply a poultice for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then wet cotton with butter, and then dress the wound with ointment until it heals;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you wish to cauterize this wound with the instrument called a 'knife', do so at the very tip, and be careful not to touch the artery in this wound which is not old.
de emigraine	of a hemorrhoid
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you are dressing a wound as we have described above in the sections on diseases, and it is not helped, and you see that neither of the cauteries mentioned earlier with medicine or with fire help, then you must heat the instrument called a  'knife' until it turns white;
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	and sign the wound with one line of about half a finger's length, and move your hand once, and cut deep enough that you do not hit the artery and reach the bone;
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and beware of the mandible that mute when one chews, and the nerve should not be affected so that it mutes and so that no spasm comes to the patient, and beware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, for cutting causes great fear especially in those who are unfamiliar with it and who are not experienced and practiced.
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and leave the work halfway through;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you in this book where it opens.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that this cautery is not sufficient for the disease and the patient suffers, cauterize him again on the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it heals.
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you see, administer the cautery which we have said in the chapter on extracting an artery, using the cautery with two knives;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and this cautery is better and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain in the ears from coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When there is pain in the ear from cold, and one has applied dissolving medicines and other remedies that we have mentioned in the previous chapter, and the pain does not go away, then heat this cautery, which is called 'the point', whose composition is as follows:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After pointing to all around the affected ear, or both ears if the pain is in both, move slightly above the root of the ear after you have marked the spot.
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and make 6 points around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then clean the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of mouth torture
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Wounds that should be cauterized are only those that cause bleeding, as we have said in the division of diseases;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not cauterize those that appear to come from dryness and nerve spasm.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you treat this type of wound that causes bleeding from fluids and discharges from the head, and gargling does not help, then you must cauterize the patient with 3 cauteries:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one at the root of the ear, and the other a little way from the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and apply the cautery to the part that appears healthy, and cauterize the top of the ear above a little below the horn of the head, and another on the temple as long as a finger;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and leave the cautery on until half of the heart is burned;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And the appearance of the scalpel that we have placed earlier, but it is a little more subtle and the knife should be a little thicker;
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After curing the site as I have said before, until it is healed.Et li chief de l’oreille metes un pic en la partie qui est entre les II levres et li nez;
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	If the apoplexy is old and you cure it as we have said, but it does not help, and the patient has a fever, then do three cauterizations:l’un en la racine dou col, et l’autre sus la nuque entre le col et la teste;et li tier entre les II mamelles;
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	II on the two horns of the head, and I in the middle of the head, and I in the place called "vessels", as we have said before, and the other cautery on the mouth of the stomach;
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and let it be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	of litharge
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this illness, one must give the patient large herbs and purging pills to cleanse the brain;
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	after washing the head of the patient thoroughly, and put on the ointment of mustard which is written in the treatise on ointments;
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is how the cautery is done:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	if you do as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If he is healed like this, it is good;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	and if he is not healed, then make three cauteries in the middle of the head going down to the neck, and space between each cautery two fingers wide;
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and treat it like the others, and if you see it fitting, and the patient is enduring, then do the cautery in the middle.
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if necessary, do the others on the two horns, and treat it until it heals.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and let the cautery be what is called "olive", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of chill from the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	The head should be cleansed of hair and of what we have said before,
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	after washing the head of the patient, then do the cautery in the middle of the head and on each horn, and behind and three times on the spine of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is enduring, and the disease is strong, then do four cauteries on the spine of the back;
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and let it be until the most of the heat has left, then lift your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	after the wound has healed, and then use the cautery called "olive oil" which we have mentioned earlier.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use cautery except for those who are phlegmatic; it is necessary first to cleanse the brain of hair and other remedies that we have discussed in the division when the patient is great and suffering from taking medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a child who cannot endure it, make a gargle and a mouthwash that purifies the brain often with good foods;
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	after the king has eaten, and then use the cautery as we have said before, and the cautery on the vessel, and on each horn;
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and if the patient is external and suffering, make a cautery as I have said for paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cautery be olive oil according to the manner that I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the disease is in a child, make him  .i. delicate cautery according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When through the cause of melancholy there are corrupt humours and thick phlegm, then cauterize it with part cauteries as we said for the one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if through the cause of melancholy the superfluities are declining towards melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give him something to drink that purifies the brain, according to what has been described before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After the king has eaten;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	Then make a well-made linen bandage, like a circle, and put it around his head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and let the patient cross his legs, and keep them well held from all sides;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	then bring forward the linen, and cut off the hair of an old bearded goat;
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and heat it gently over the fire so that the patient can withstand the heat when he drinks from the bottle;
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	then empty the bladder within through the neck, and let it cool;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this to the patient once every week with good management until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or, if you want to cauterize it all over, make several small points on the end of the cautery tool.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This cautery moistens the brain greatly;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then put on cotton wet with goat's milk and wax.
de l’awe des eulz	of their eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When awesomeness first comes to the eyes due to the signs I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient drink that cleanses the head, and guard it from all moisture, and make them sweat in a bath several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	Then he instructs the patient to lower his head, and he applies the cautery on his head, and performs 2 cauteries on the 2 temples if the decline of the eye is in both, or just one if it's only in one;
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	and cover all the veins and arteries below the heart with the cautery, and let the cautery be as long as the width of the temple;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	and beware of bleeding, and if you see too much blood issue, then stop it with some clay powder as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you in the extraction of the arteries and the incision cautery how you should stop it;
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	and sometimes they make cauterization or incision under the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the body from tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When tears are old and accustomed, and on the veins, or within the arteries that lie near the appearance of the head outside;
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and it is seen that these are cold phlegmatic excesses, then you must do the cautery I mentioned earlier in the descending awl into the eyes:
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	I cauterize inside the head, and 2 cauteries on the 2 temples, and 2 cauteries under the 2 bones;
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	and if there is more need, then cauterize the eye socket above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	where the body weeps inside them
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you have treated him according to what we have said in the section, and he does not improve, then give the patient three nights of bleeding;
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	afterwards bleed the head, and cauterize it with a cautery of olive oil;
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and make two cauteries with a cautery called "clavis" above the two eye sockets, a little below the hairline;
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and be careful of the artery that you do not pierce it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the membrane of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize it with the tool called "olive".
de coi ci est li forme:	It should be shaped in the following way:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see fit, make two cauteries above the eye sockets as long as the eyebrows are;
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not remove your hand until the third part of the paper is burnt, according to the manner I have described.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair that pokes the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	At times the hair of the eyelids turns white, pricking the eye, and cauterization is performed in two ways:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	that is, with fire or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne,
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein;and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die. When they grow and are even, then put the patient in water; after that, draw on paper the shape of an eyeball, as well as the beginning of the sign from among the hairs;Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then I wet cotton with egg white and fennel seed paste on the eye, then heat the cautery so that it is the right shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After that, cauterize little by little over the shape you have marked, a little bit at a time, until the ulcer is burned in that place;
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the sign of health is when you see the papery skin retracted, and the hairs standing up at the edge of the eye;
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	then take your hand away, and leave it like that for three days; then wet cotton with butter to cool the burn.
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if afterwards the hairs come back, and the papery skin is soft again, then start the cautery process over from the beginning, just as you did before.
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	and if the hairs are broken off, cauterize it so that the paper lifts to its natural level, and is even, and does not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The burning cautery of medicine is what you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a parchment in the shape of a myrtle leaf;
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	then take French soap and quicklime, of each one part, and grind them well together;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and make it into a paste quickly so that it does not cool, then spread it over the parchment in the shape of the myrtle leaf, and place the hairs on top;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the disease is only in one eye, then operate on that one, and if it is in both, then operate on both;
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and place under the eye moistened cotton in egg white;
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	and the head of the sick person is in great pain and puts his hand on the medicine, and presses it and moves it every time the patient feels biting from the medicine, because he feels the biting as much as fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from your hand.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the biting is passed, raise the area, and look if you see the paper raised as it was raised by the constraint of fire or by incision;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if so, it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not, then apply more medicine to the area where the medicine did not take effect, until your work is even and the eyes are in their proper place;
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put on wet cotton dipped in butter until the wound heals, after cleaning the area of the ointment which is called 'diaphenes' and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to take care of your work very carefully so that it does not leak into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes soft afterward, and the hair pricks in the eye, then restart the medicine on that area which has been softened by the paper properly, just as you did before.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the cure until it is healed;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and this is the shape of the blister:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that men's eyes are diverse in size and smallness, and according to that are your constraints;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and the true way is not known to him whose study this art is.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	on the treatment of fistula with cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have described in the sections on diseases, and your treatments are not effective, then you should use cautery according to the following method:
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to put his head in your lap;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and let the surgeon hold his head between his hands in such a way that he does not move or drop his head;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	afterwards, put wet cotton in egg white or in parsley juice on the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	then heat the cautery which is made thus:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	is shaved at the top so that it is shaped like a quill, along with which the cautery is held;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you see it pointed from one end to the other, and if you see it as flat as a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but nonetheless, the one that is shaved is best for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	Afterwards, press the fistula if it is open, and treat the pus, and dry it;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if it is closed, open it and treat the bowels;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	afterwards, put on the hot cautery, and hold your hand at the cautery near the corner of the eye, so that your hand does not make a mistake;
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and place the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of cautery up to the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, then use the cautery again, and if you need another one, leave it for 3 days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	after moistening cotton in butter, and the poultice of a drying ointment until it is healed, and if 40 days pass without healing, then apply the medicine of corrosive water until the bone is uncovered;
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and treat according to how it behaves in its own chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula that some of the ancients spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	When treating a fistula, locate and open the passage;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	afterwards, insert into the slit one-sixth of a bean of what it was formed from;
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and make it the size of a pea;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand on the bean firmly so that the patient does not move, and so that the pus does not flow to the eye;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and one should moisten cotton in wine or water and place it on the eye of the patient;
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	the bean then opens the passage of the fistula, and heals by a marvellous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery we mentioned, that is good.Si li fistule ne fuist saine, et met en la fendure un pafre de fer de coi li fistule est venuz, et le met tant que li pafre soit en la fistule.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If the fistula is not healed, insert an iron probe into the opening from which the fistula has emerged, and push it in until the probe is inside the fistula. If that doesn't work, you must administer an enema to the nose, and bring the fistula back towards the nose according to where it should be in its proper location.
des crevaices en levres	of cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, cracks occur on the lips which are called "hair", and especially on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as we have described in the sections, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small scalpel according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And he applies cauterization to these fissures until it reaches the bone;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards, treat the area with ointment until it heals.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess forms at the root of the gum or uvula, or palate, or tooth roots, it causes swelling and suppuration, and becomes ulcerated and turns into a fistula.
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have described in the section on incisions, but it does not help:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	therefore, you must use cauterization according to the size of the fistula.
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	afterwards, heat the iron and apply it to the opening of the fistula, holding your hand steady so that the hot iron touches the bottom of the wound.
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this once or twice, afterwards treating it as we have described for healing wounds, until it is healed.
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if it is cured thus, it is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if not, then one must uncover the area and remove the corrupted bone, according to how you find it in its joint.
dou movement des dens	movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine but it does not help, then put the head of the patient in your lap:
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	after heat up the cautery which will be described below in such a way that you place a candle on top of the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and hold the hot cautery in your hand until the patient feels the heat going to the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	then lift your hand and repeat the cautery as you wish;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	then fill the patient's mouth with salt water and let it sit for an hour and spit often.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way, the tooth which was loose is made firm, and the soft gums restrained, and the corrupted moisture dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When toothache comes from cold, or there is coldness or paleness, and medical treatments don't work, then cautery is needed in two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Butter cautery is such that you heat butter from a cow, and the tip in a spoon made of iron or bronze;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	Afterwards, take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a tent pole, and moisten it in the butter, and place it on the aching tooth until it is cool;
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	And in this way, do it often until its power reaches the root of the tooth; and if you see the butter-soaked wool and cotton getting cold, and place it on the aching tooth, and hold the hot iron close to the gum of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The fire cautery together is such that you take an iron or bronze rod, and it should be thick so that the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient;
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After heating the cautery, from which the form will come, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, for the pain will be relieved that day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary for the patient to fill his mouth with good butter quickly after this cautery, and then rinse it out.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And here is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make a cautery of whatever you like, according to what you have power over;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and this is the form of the dog's tooth:
des scrophules	of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When scrofula is of phlegmatic and cold moisture, and does not respond to digestion through medicine, then heat the cautery blade, as shown in the illustration, with two openings for the smoke to emerge from the other side of the cautery;
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and place the hot cautery blade once on the abscess where it is needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to the size of the abscess and leave it for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and place wet cotton in butter over the burn until the burn is healed;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the area with ointments and bandages until it is completely healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When moisture prevails over the channels of the stomach, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient should be purged first with medicines that loosen the bowels.
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	After this, make a cautery at the root of the throat, and be careful not to go too far into the throat, but only burn it lightly near the heart.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After this, make another cautery at the joint of the neck at the head of the spine, and use the cautery called 'clavicle' as described earlier.
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	And treat the area until it is healed, as described earlier.Quant li chief de l’espinee est mal adjoigniez a la base dou chief, et li membres li plus ne se muevent
de la toust	of the tongue
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When the top of the spine is misaligned with the base of the head and the limbs do not move freely, and all diseases of the stomach are due to cold moisture, and the patient does not have a fever or dryness, and it is an old disease, then make the cauteries on the nerves as described earlier.
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and another cautery in between the two breasts;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and let the cautery, which is called "clavicle," be according to the form that has been described earlier.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see fit, make a cautery on the spot with the cautery, which is called "pinpoint," according to the form described earlier in the ailment of the ears;
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and let there be 30 points or more around it.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	Afterwards heal the place according to what was said before, and let the cauteries be in three lines according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And for this reason, cauteries are gentler when you do them three times.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Afterwards, the patient should be bled on their back and ribs;et li sang qui venoit de lor costeit entor et li col, qu’il soit retre
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	and the blood that comes from their ribs around their neck and throat, let it be gently pressed after gently lifting the sternum with your left hand's fingers;et soit li sang qui venoit de lor costeit entor et li col,
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated inside, scorch the cautery which has the nerves of the eyes, and here is the form:et soit li sang qui venoit de lor costeit entor et li col, qu’il soit retre
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the vein until it is completely cut, and the figure of the cautery comes out together with four cauteries;
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and for this reason cautery is made with the cautery that has three strings, so that the figures of cauterization are six cauteries;
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and the nerves follow the subtlety of a tent and this is the shape of the cautery that has three strings:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes it is adjusted above this one nerve, so that there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	After, put on the cautery small pieces of silk;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterwards, let the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is well healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, which happens rarely, then make cautery on the thick part of the cautery-clavicle, or many cauteries in points.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and moisture is eliminated and the illness is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and moisture come into the stomach, causing pain to its nature, and there are many catarrhs in him, and he does not benefit from customary treatments, then you must pour water on his back, and stretch out his legs and arms.And if he vomits with difficulty, do the same.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	After that, do three cauteries under the nail of the big toe, one cautery in the middle and two cauteries on either side so that the figures of the cauteries are at three angles, with an equal space between them so they do not touch when they bend due to pus;
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and the cautery marks are so deep that they mark both parts of the chest, and the shape of the cauteries follows this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you want to cauterize a large area in the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and whoever fears this cautery, cauterize a small area and sign on the stomach with one dot according to how much you want to do;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then cauterize it with what is called a 'point'.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the wound we have described above, once it has healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When the liver hurts from cold and moisture and excess flatulence, so much that it is out of its natural condition;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the disease is cured by what we have said in divisions, and if it does not help, the patient must be bled on his vein;
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and sign three cauteries according to this form and shape and quantity on the liver, avoiding the hypochondrium, where the ribs of man come;
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and there must be a space between each cautery equal to the thickness of two fingers;
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and the cauteries should be held lightly on the body, and do not press hard with your hand on the entire cautery;
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	and only the half of the cautery should be burned, and the patient should be laid straight on his back;
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if he cannot lie flat, then let him lie on his side, and stretch out his legs and lift up his hips;
et c’est li forme:	and here is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if you wish, cauterize these cauteries of the cupping glass, if you are skillful and wise in the art, and be careful not to burn all over the body, for then you would dry out the whole body;
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and do not go too deep, because the skin is very delicate there, and you can tell by looking.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When he has an abscess in his liver, and you want to know whether it is in the meat of the liver or in the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	if it is in the meat, the patient feels pain not too strongly;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	and if it is in the membrane, he feels intense pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And then when this treatment has been applied to the abscesses, the patient should be laid on his back;
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then sign with your finger on the spot where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is similar to a reed, so that it is red hot;
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	and cauterize with the cautery until the abscess is burnt, and goes as far as the membrane, until all the pus is driven out;
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the treatment, dress the wound until it is healed;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	and no one should ever use this cautery except someone who has studied the art of medicine for a long time, and through whose hands these diseases have sometimes been cured.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore he can work boldly, and nevertheless it seems to me that it is better to leave it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of a cautery of phlegmon
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancients said that one must do cauterizations to the warts with roots of aristolochia, and in such a manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	take a root of aristolochia that is long, the largest one you can find, and dried, and as thick and long as your finger.
