et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and one of the incisions as deep as two fingers right in the middle of the forehead going down, and the other two on either side above the eyelids, and be careful not to cut into the arteries that are on either side above the eyelids;
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and keep your hand away from the jaw, and let each incision be as deep as three fingers across the joints;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have ready a piece of sponge and a lot of linen to wipe up the blood, then insert the spatulum, split into two parts as shown in the figure:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	from the incision which is cut from the temple all the way to the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and scrape all the flesh which is between the two cuts all the way to the sinus that is over the bone, then do likewise from the middle cut all the way to the other second one, and then pull out this spatulum.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Then insert into the first incision the instrument that is called  "cultellary", and it is very sharp on one side, and not at all sharp on the other, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And cut the coat according to the shape of the chest, and the lower part towards the bone, and bring it together until it reaches the middle slit.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head into the eye socket until the incision is continuous all the way to the sinus, and then likewise do in the middle cut all the way to the other one outside;
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then draw out the blood equally, and express the place where the blood is taken from;Et s’il avint qu’en l’un des II cotés il soit si grant dolor que li malsens ne
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	then put into each wound a tent of old cotton, and place over it wet cloths soaked in wine, oil, and garlic, and be careful that hot abscesses do not develop.
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	On the third day, loosen the bandage and give him a large drink of cold water, then treat the wound with basilicon ointment mixed with rose oil, and other remedies used for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	from the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When someone has a catarrh and you see their eyes are sunken and small, and their vision is weakened, and the eyelids are burned:
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hair falls out, and they feel pain in the head, and the sick person sneezes;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	then you may know from these signs that those materials and this catarrh come from many veins, and the mother's milk is what it is, and so it is cured.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you must instruct the patient to look straight ahead, then make a large slit in the forehead, and another one from the corner of the eye.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begin from the left temple to the right temple, and make the incision all the way to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and keep your hand away from the nerves in the temples that control swallowing;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is exposed, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, and then pack between the two lips of the incision cotton wool and linen bandages;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then apply dampened fabrics in wine and oil, and beware of a hot abscess;
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	when it is removed, you should rub the bone until it begins to form a callus, then treat it with drying agents that promote the hardening of new bone.
En teil maniere:	In this way:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	take two parts of flour of wheat, and four parts of colofoint, and make a poultice of it;
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and administer it to these wounds to promote healing throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the treatment of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	All that which falls out from the ears is one of four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	or beans, or a beast, or a stone from a mine, or something similar like iron;
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seeds such as peas, beans, and lentils;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or flowing substances such as water, oil, and vinegar, and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear, whether a pebble or something else that does not adhere to the ear nor grow in it, one must hold the ear towards the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see a stone, then distil some violet oil or oil of mastic, and then apply an extractant;Si est beste, s’il li traveist la piere, si distille l’oile sus l’enduit, ou si li traveit la beste, si dist
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	If it is a beast, if the stone pierces through, then distil the oil on the wound, or if the beast bites him, distil and cause sneezing with a condiment, and stop the nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put a piece of cloth or wool around the ear;Si est semence, si enduit li pueilz de l’oreille et met l’espece de la sem
et estent l’oreille au desus.	If it is a seed, anoint the lobes of the ear and put the species of the seed on top.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Many times comes out by this cure;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come out, then administer extraction with delicate tweezers, of which there is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it pops out with the tweezers, that's good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	if not, then administer extraction with a small, thin needle;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it does not come out with that, then make a small needle of bronze and push the tip of the needle into the ear canal firmly, and pack around the needle with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the needle;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	then pull it out gently, because many times it comes out as we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if it does not come out in such a way, then take tweezers and grab the object, and place some instrument that is suitable for doing so, and put a little cotton around it;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	then press the buttocks against the stone or whatever it is, and pull out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	If it does not come out from all these things we have said, then quickly split the ear so that the abscess, callus, and spasm can come out;
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	and the way to make the split is that you first bleed the patient from the head, and draw blood according to its strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn his ear upwards, and cut a small opening at the root of the ear into the fat where it depends;
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and the incision should be like a moon, as you go to the stone, then suck it energetically with your mouth;
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	treat until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it is a graze that is in and it swells, then administer extraction;
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if it cannot emerge, then administer Spatula tenui subtilis according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision on that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do this when you think the graze is moist due to moisture from the ear, until you have made many pieces;
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then extract it with tweezers and with a suction device, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water that drains from the ear, the patient should first sneeze with snuff, and plug the ear with cotton wool.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	Let him lie on the same side as the ear ache is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	if it jumps out by itself, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	if not, then take many small stones according to the length of your finger, thin and light, and heat them slightly in the fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and I put a hole in the patient's ear, and pierce it from another part of his foot, and pierce another stone on the stone that is in the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and do not stop piercing stone with stone until all the pus flows out, and so it will flow out completely;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you see that they take a straw and insert one end into the ear, and the other end is held to the fire until the most painful part of the straw is burned;
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then do the same with other straws until all the pus flows out, as we have said for the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In removing a foreign object from an animal, if it is of a small body, such as a flea and similar objects, remove it as we have said in the division;
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is of a large body that can be felt, then use tweezers to extract it;et s’il est si petit qu’il ne soit nule part senti, si prend asche, et frotte li chiés
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and it is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the section on distillations, and the treatment is ineffective, then you should examine the ear in the sunlight:
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	if no worms appear, then pinch the ear lobes gently; if none emerge, then take a small needle and pierce where the shape of the worm is visible:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow below and broad above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	and insert the thinnest end into the ear according to the amount of pain the patient is experiencing, then suck firmly on the needle;
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	do this repeatedly until all the worms emerge.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not come out, then stop up the ear with cotton as I have said regarding stones;
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not emerge as described, then administer the distillations that the ancients have experimented with for worm removal, and you will find them in the section on distillations;
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all this apparatus, from which is the shape as you see it:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And whether it is of silver or bronze, there should be a small hole underneath and a larger hole above for distillation;
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and to press the distillation into the apparatus, made of well-crafted bronze, and if you see fit, take a razor and wrap it around the point with cotton;
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you desire from your medicines into the canal, and the canal should be in the ear;
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	then put the razor wrapped in cotton inside, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled into the ear canal;
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillation be heated over fire so that it may be distilled into the ear;
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and be sure it is not too cold, for the medicine would not then be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the treatment of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born without ears;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and the same thing happens in adults through punctures of the ear, or by a boil forming inside the ear, and sometimes this swelling goes right into the ear, so that it cannot be seen;
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and sometimes there is only slight damage to the eardrum, which can be seen quite clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	When the eardrum is punctured and cannot be seen, it is a serious condition in many cases, and when one can see it, you should expose the ear of the patient to the sun;
et regarde dedens:	and look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the membrane exposed, then treat it in the following way:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And it should be sharp and smooth all around so that it does not pierce the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	if the operation is on the skin of the ear, hold it with fine pincers and lift gently until the skin is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the obstructions are deep in the ear, then take a thin, light scalpel and heat it gently in the fire, then place it on the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the operation on the skin, pierce it gently and be careful not to cut into the nerves of the ear;
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	then put in the ear a tent according to the size of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this for several days until the wound is healed, or take a tent and moisten it with rose water, and dust with ground vitriol;
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and if you see swelling in the ear, it is necessary to remove the tent and replace it with another tent moistened with cerotic ointment made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then dress the wound until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if there is bleeding, take a sponge and cloth dipped in cold water and apply it to the ear, and use other remedies that stop the bleeding that are used for distilling.
de la char des papieres	of paper charcoal
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	This treatment comes from papers made of them when they are moist and dry; you should extend them with tweezers and pincers, and the edge of a spatula from its roots.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Then place powdered vitriol over the area.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if there is skin in it, then cauterize with a delicate lens-shaped cautery instrument, and the cauterizer after the incision is worth a mouse.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	And many times they return, as long as nothing remains of their roots.
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times there come from the papers things that look like gravel in form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "gout", and it is a gathering of thick moisture above and below the paper.
li ovraiges est telz:	such are the tasks:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	take care that the warts do not move from one place to another, and this is an easy thing to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	then make a deep cut in it, then scrape each part lightly with a knife, and then grab it with tweezers and pull it out.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	if you cannot pull it out without piercing the skin a little, do not worry about hurting the patient;
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	and if the wound is large, then sew it up and treat it until it heals;
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	and if it is small, do not use force, as the oil will restore it immediately and heal it.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the wart is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, turn it over and grab the wart with tweezers, and then pull it out while pressing from both sides;
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the paper is removed by the incision, it does not matter.
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the wound is healed, wash with salt water and treat the area around the eye until the patient is cured.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a fat that collects in the membranes above the eyelids, and this happens most often to children, and it causes them great pain, and in the mornings they have catarrh, and they cannot bear to look at sunlight because their tears flow into their eyes.
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	And because of this they lie down and sleep with their faces covered, and their eyelids become moist and puffy, and the appearance is concealed by the exinach that protrudes into the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the eye with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the manner of the operation is for the patient to put his head on the operator's lap;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains out-pushing from each part, then put it on him;
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press with your fingers on either side so that the out-pushing is gathered within the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then cut in the middle of the moisture with the spatula a slit as wide as the wound that is made when opening a vein;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and cut through the skin to the depth until you reach the out-pushing;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in many cases out-pushing comes from the slit according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Pull it out then with tweezers between your fingers, turning your hand to the right and left until it is stretched;
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and be careful not to push into the slit so that you do not touch the spatula to the eye and harm it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the wound does not open at the beginning of the incision, then increase the incision slightly until it opens.
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	Then extract as we have said, then moisten bandages in vinegar and water, and place them on the wound, and use bandages to hold it in place.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind sesame seeds and place them on top to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the eye until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is a hot abscess in the eye, treat it with soothing poultices until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	And if a cold abscess comes to the area, apply a hot poultice until it is warm; then apply warm oil, and treat it with bandages.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When hairs grow on paper, different from their natural state, and they are damaged, it harms them, and causes various diseases, like tears, and softening of the paper and the skin, until it becomes the cause of their destruction.
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	And there are three ways to treat this:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	Either by fire cautery, or by using a medicine according to what is in the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and stitching, or by splints, according to what I will say.Et la cause de la destruction des poilz est par le feu ou par medicine de cautere, selonc ce qu’il avient en la nature de la maladie:
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	You should place the patient's head on your lap, then turn the paper over their eye to your left hand.
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	If it is converted, that is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if not, then put an needle on the thread above it.
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and let him hold the margin of the paper where the hairs grow next to these hairs, and draw the thread above it all the way up to the paper, then turn it back to the razor.
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	Then he should cut under the paper, under the hair, all along the spatulum, from the large to the small.
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	Then pull out the thread and place a small piece of cotton and linen under the paper, then draw an inch-long figure on the paper in the shape of a mirtle leaf, and according to the amount that you see the paper rising, you should make it longer or shorter.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if it has a great quantity of paper according to how the paper is softened;
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	then do the whole spatula-like on the two lines you have signed, and start from the large to the small;
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and be one of the slits close to the natural hair in the thickness of a root, then insert the needle into one of the two corners of the heart, then scrape it all;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then assemble the two lips with a stitch of a fine woolen thread, and draw out the blood, and dry the excess of the threads above the two eyelids with any sticky thing, if you want to do this;
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if not, then don't worry about it, then leave the stitch and threads for three or four days;
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	then cure the wound without stitches with dry and compressing things, for the paper rises to the soudainness of the wound and its gathering, but the stitch is painful (as the ancients say), and it is work without fear;
et si a une autre maniere:	and if there is another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and you should draw the paper in the shape of a leaf of myrtle, as we have described, with three lobes evenly spaced according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut out what is above with small scissors evenly according to the shape which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you cannot hold the tweezers and the object is not even, then take a needle and thread and sew it into the figure:
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	And sew another thread through the large eyelet, and the second thread through the small one, and bring the threads together evenly between your fingers:
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then lift your hand evenly, and lift up all the skin above which you have sewn, as we have described, then bring together the two lips of the wound by stitching, and heal it until it is healthy:
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if an abscess comes from your incision, then soothe it with cerots and similar soothing ointments:
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and sometimes the hairs of the paper are converted:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	if you should use that which we have said about the incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The cure of bones is as follows:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and you should convert the paper and insert it according to what I have said, and then make two bones by art, and two thin ligaments as long as the paper and the broadness of the spleen is;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and cut into two parts where you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then assemble one and the other sutilly above what stands out from the paper of the eye, and draw out the two bones from the two formed parts;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and let it be thus for a few days, and the skin that is stretched will die and shrivel and fall off as it drops off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it is delayed, then treat it with cautery until it is healed.
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound is sutured and the skin raised, then the hairs will no longer prick.
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	And this is the form of the two cans that you shall make according to this figure and this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	The tools are such that you thread a thin needle with fine silk;
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then bring the heads together and tie them subtly together, and the length of the threads should be a palm long;
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then place in the hollow another fine thread of silk, and tie the heads of the thread;
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	then put the patient's head into the hole;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and it should be done under the sun so that the procedure is visible, for it is a subtle and small procedure; then push the needle all the way into the root of the hair, piercing the skin gently until you reach the natural hair;
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	then pull out the hair up to the root, and put into the socket that hair, if there are one or two or three or more;
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	then pull your hand back so that the hairs grow straight into the socket with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the socket is treated and the hair does not grow out with it, then you shall pull the socket from below to the very end of the thread that you tied to it, until the socket comes out through the hole above, and you see it through your eye.
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	then you shall pull on the socket and the thread, closing your eye for two or three days, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh grows over it;Et si la chasse est trop foible que tu ne puisses la traire ains se rompt le fil, si mettrais la cheville de l’un costat et la cheville de l’auter en celui auter costat qu’il soit leu, tant
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	and if the hairs are short, then accompany it with a long hair from the tail of a horse, and let it grow along with it until it is elongated, and then release it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the eye's pus
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this disease called "aleacrati" or warts comes on the eye, there are two ways in which it occurs:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	One is natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or cutting or cauterization, and by similar means.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the manner of the treatment for this is to split the wart, and separate its lips, and place in it flax threads, and let it stay until it heals.
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And one must not use in its treatment anything that dries and constricts.Et si li porriture est innatureil, si tu les esprenges a l’huile d’olives et a l’huile d’am
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do that, the disease will return worse than before;And s’el est en la paume de la main ou de la pie, si covient qu’
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but treat with softening things, such as fenugreek;
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and use rosewater or water heated and seeded with flax, and apply a poultice of softened pig fat, and treat the area with ointments made from a variety of oils, and cover it with a tent, and apply a hot compress to the area.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And in your treatment, be sure that you do not allow it to heal according to its previous shape;
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and the treatments we have described are for this condition alone, so that it does not return to its previous shape.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease, which is beneath what is truly called "the brain", is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	Accidents come from wounds, incisions, cauterization, and similar things;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	and the way to treat it is to take a needle and thread it with a double strand of thread, then insert the needle into the flesh and pass it through from one side of the wound to the other, so that the thread passes through both sides of the wound;
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	then they are sewn up at the top all along the needle, and the cone is made wide at the spatulate end.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the shape of the parchment returns as it should, that is good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	if not, then take a razor and put it in the slit, and turn the parchment over, and make two slits along the inside of the parchment;
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and the head of the two slits are at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and an angle is made so that when they are put together, the shape is like that of a letter which has the form «I griesche»;
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	then remove this thread, according to the amount that its sides are stretched below, from that which follows the parchment, then join the two severed parts and sew them together with a thread of wool;
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with what we have said about softening medications and bandages until he is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the illness comes from a tear or a cut or cautery, then you must make a clean cut under the hair of the scalp, and according to what is said above:
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	then separate the two lips of the tent as I have said;
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and the treatment should be according to the form of the disease, for it is very different in form, and the wise master doctor prepares an instrument with all his skill so that the form returns to its natural shape;
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the illness itself, according to what it needs in terms of treatment and instruments, in many different ways.
dou soudement de la papiere	suddenly from the scalp
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this soudure happens to adult men in such a way that the scalp above is separated from the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must stick the tip of a razor under the scalp and lift it upward;
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and they stretch them as far as they can withstand the subtle spatulum, neither too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient cannot endure the pain of a spatulum that is too sharp or cuts the eye;
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and your incision, by which you scrape that union, should be light, so that the membrane returns according to its natural shape;
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and all that union is cleaned, and sometimes in the eye there is salty pus, and it is raised with fresh water and collarets;
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	then place a piece of linen between the membrane and the eye, and place over the eye wool moistened in egg white;
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and after three days use collarets and sudoric things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the eyelid
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	You should know that the nail has two manners:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	one is nervous and resembles a hard wart, and the other is not nervous but resembles frozen white moisture; when touched with iron, it feels numb to the fingers, yet no one can feel it.the first manner is when there is a vein beneath it; the second manner is when it has no vein beneath it, but is flat like a membrane.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	and both the appearance begins towards the great tear duct, and grows little by little until it covers all the view and all the light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the manner of the incision is such that the patient puts his head in the air, then he works them;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and lightly take the paper in your hand, then curl it with your nails as pincers of small doublet, and hold them on top;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and put on it a horse's hair, or cow's, or ox's, and strong thread;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the point of the needle a little and push it into the nail, and pierce all the way through the needle, and tie the nail with thread and hold them on top, and scrape along the side of the nail which follows the tear duct to the edge of the eyelid and attach the thread to the hair just above the tear duct, then cut off the remainder at the root of the tear duct all the way to the tear gland gently and with small forces, and leave the natural skin on the tear duct so that through the incision doesn't come the accustomed flesh;
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and sometimes the nails are affected at the nailbed only, and along the nail, as we have said;
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	then they scrape away all of the scaly skin that is the cause of this condition.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And be careful that the scaly skin does not touch and break the delicate flesh, and that the fingernail is not pierced;
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after making the incision, pour a little quicksilver into the wound, and apply a collar made of litharge, leaving it on until the next day;
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it as needed until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not sensitive and you cannot push in a needle, and the nailbed will not allow entry, many times this kind of nail has been cured by medicines;
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and they grow back as I have described in the section on division; and if you see it covering up again, treat the nailbed according to the illness, taking the scaly skin gently with a sharp tool according to this method:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And raise the nail gently, and if you see that it does not lessen and the pus is forced out, then distil from your mouth into the eye a collar made of litharge and red copper dust, and seal the eye until the next day.
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Then restart the other treatment according to this same method, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then milk it, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then begin the work again as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the flesh around the eye damages it greatly, then suspend it at the eyelid, and scrape away a part of it but not all, so that no body of tears comes to it.
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	Then distil into the eye a red collar made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which grows on the eyeball
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	In some men's eyes, a red vein sometimes emerges and covers the pupil and constricts it, and then retreats into the back of the eye, resembling a rose made of brass.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	and the work is such that the patient puts his head on yours, then he works them, and pulls all that flesh to hooks suitable for this, and holds it with strength;
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	then shave the first part of the flesh, and go all along shaving to the end, and be careful not to cut the eye during the operation;
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and let the incision be from the spleen to that which we have said in the incision of the fingernail, and with small forces from which one removes the stone, as the form after this chapter demonstrates;
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is complete and all the flesh removed, then apply the eye of silk thread in which you distil red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines, and place over it cotton wool soaked in egg white, so that it is secured from hot abscesses;
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if nothing remains there, and the cold blood flows over it, and you doubt a hot abscess, then leave the eye and treat the abscess with things that soothe hot abscesses;
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do as much as is adjusted in the eye by this appearance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	However, you should still lighten the treatment of each weak eye through the natural way;
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and of the accidental way, in the work of iron;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this member can bear that work.
des voines des eulz	of veins of them
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Veins are red lines that cover the eye, they hinder vision and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	So it is necessary for the first thing you look at the eye, in which way it is, and out of which there is no other disease but the evil;
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then treat it in such a way:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient to put his head down, then open those veins gently according to his wisdom, and let the veins be subtle and double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two edges be gradual in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then open those veins strongly, and draw out the blood hour after another, until you see those veins removed from the eye;
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and be careful not to hurt the eye with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very cautious in your work so that you do not miss any veins.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	And when you have finished, distill into the eye a green and red collyrium to corrupt what is remaining of the infection.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you are unable to draw out everything in that hour, then apply an ointment to the eye of things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it for a few days until the pain is eased and the abscess is secured with a hot poultice, then begin again according to the method described above until it is healed.
et c’est li forme des forces:	And this is the formula of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the eye fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The physician called "Arisati" treated a fistula:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	when you have treated it with cautery and medicine of fire according to what I have said above, and it is not healed, then there is an infection in it that you must cut open over the abscess, where it should be, and draw out all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is uncovered, and you will see the decay and blackness, then take all the tools with which this is formed;
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and it is called 'asparagus', and it should be made of iron into a small head, and pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And put on the location of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little bit until you know that the corruption is gone;
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do this several times, then restore the place with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	if the place is sewn up, and the flesh grows together, and the body of the wound is sewn up, and remains like this for 40 days, and it does not open again and no evil accident comes, then you may know that it is healed;
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	If not, there is no other remedy but to bring the fistula back to the opening of the ear according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	And it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered, he takes the forest according to this form, and the head of the iron should be three-pointed, and the shaft should be thinned down to its tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	Then he places it on the bone near the eardrum, and he removes his hand from the ear, then he returns to pushing the iron in until it pierces the bone, and the patient feels it through his eardrum if he keeps his hand over his ear.
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	And then it is healed with dry remedies as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens, he checks the matter in the ear.
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the output of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eyes are fully open all around and there is no disturbance or diminution, then you must ligature the patient;
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then cleanse the eye, then apply leeches or a hot poultice without burning to suck out the humor, then place on the eye an ointment made of acacia, aloe, incense, and myrrh, and then bind it up with bandages and cloths; and if it is a child,
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the manner of the cloths is that you fold soft cloths in half, and double each one in four, and then place them one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye needs; and if it is a child,
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	then bind it firmly from above with a hard bandage, and reapply the leeches to suck without burning;and if there is still humor,then take a needle and pierce the eye at its upper corner,and apply the leeches again to suck out the humor.Then, place on the eye an ointment made
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	then remove the cupping glasses and leave the eye stretched day and night, and if the ligatures loosen, you must stretch it a lot.
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	then remove the bandage after a day and a night, and if you see the eye healing, that's good;
se ce non;	if not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	then restart the poultice and bandages and the ligature and cupping glasses until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	from the rupture of a woven fabric
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When a disruption occurs in the woven web, then it opens up, and something like a grain of resin comes out, and it is terrible to see;
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	then, if you see it covering up, the treatment is such that you push a needle into the root of the part below up to the part above, then push another needle where there is a double thread on the eyelid;
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and have it pierced, and leave the first needle in place according to its position;
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	Then cut the thread of a double-threaded needle and tie one end around the eye, and tighten it well, then pull out the needle and place the moistened other eye on top.
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and let it be until the thread breaks with the eye, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed;
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and sometimes the wound is restrained by the eye on each side of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eyes appear large, then pierce them with a fine spatulum which comes from the depth of the eye, and scrape away the white moisture and lower the eyes, and enter immediately;
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then pull it out until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the corner of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease called 'alkunati' has no cure except by removing the film that gathers in the eye, resembling descending water, but it is not water;
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the way to perform this operation is as follows: make the patient sit on a chair that is prepared and straight, then take the head in your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the jaw coming up to your eyes.
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then be quiet, and lower the light, and look at the patient's face as usual;
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not go away, you know it is acute, and if the jaw' going down is not as we have described.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	make the patient sit between your hands, then take the spatula and gently press on the membrane above the corner of the eye with the conjunctiva and the membrane, until the jaw releases.
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it is released, put in the eye hot water mixed with honey, or boiling water or fenugreek and honey, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have already described the appearances of diseases in their various forms, and what is necessary to know about them.
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	act according to the instructions regarding health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	You should make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light and towards the sun, and then close his healthy eye and squeeze it firmly.
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	Then place the paper on the eye with your left hand if the eyes are on the left, or with your right hand if they are on the right;
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	Then take in your right hand, if the eyes are on the left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand if they are on the right;
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Then place the tip of the instrument below the white part of the eye near the inner corner, and then push the "almagda" gently and twist your hand so that it pierces the white of the eye, feeling for the empty space;
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and the measure of the path of the alchemy should be at the bottom of the measure of the space which is from the prunelle to the end of the darkness;
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and it is the crown of the eye;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	if you see the bone in that paper because of the clarity of the horned tissue, then put the instrument in the place where the water is, and then express it under one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if he sees the water now, let the patient see it before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After a little rest, if the water rises up the second path, put it back with the instrument, and when it is stuck in and no longer rising, gently draw out the alchemy by turning your hand a little bit at a time;
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then put in a little gem oil, and remove that eye from inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by force into the eye cotton wool or linen moistened in rose oil and an abundance of egg white, and bind it with clean cloth.Si li aigue ne vout point remonier, si leve la fuer de dedans la vierne et de l’oil avec un picquet de fer ou d’oile de paume et legierement avec un puitier de fer; puis li lie avec l’oil sain.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	If the water does not want to rise again, then lift the force from within the vein and eye with an iron rod or palm oil and gently with an iron spoon; then bind it with clean cloth. We, and those who are of our time, put on ground cumin mixed with an abundance of egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if  'almagda' cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some people whose eyes are too hard, then you should take the instrument called  'alberit', which has this shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And so pierce the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make the place subtle, then put in the alchemy as we have said;
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	and at the completion of the work, prepare for the patient by bringing to him a bed in a dark place where he can sleep on his back.
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and let him abstain from all movement and eat light foods, and not move his head or to the right or left, and let him be bound according to his condition for three days.
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	Then release him in that same dark house and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then remove the bandage by the seventh day.
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And you should not do this during the hour of the treatment or after an incision is made, but you should alleviate it, because the water rises rapidly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	If a hot abscess comes, release the eye before the seventh day, and use that which soothes an abscess;
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	and when it is appeased, he looses the bandage and puts a blindfold over his eyes to cover them, and then he is led into that dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	Then he leaves the house little by little, and returns to his senses;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and know that no student should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us from the Land of Israel, who told us that in his land they make almond milk, which is sucked out by a tube, but I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read about it in ancient books;
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and perhaps it is a new thing.Et je vis de la mesme aigue fere un pou monia, si que
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the similarities of the forms of almonds, so that those who do not know them may see them;
et soient d’arain proprement:	and they are properly of bronze:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the heads of the needles have this same subtlety, and the hindmost are pointed in three angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart through the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	There are times when children are born with various deformities, and among them there are some who look like scorpions with feet.
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if they have a wound of flesh-colored hue, and if they have a sore of boney color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	For those who have sores and not wounds, you should make the patient sit in your hands facing the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	open his nose, and pour oil on the sores, and draw it out;
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	then hold what you can sustain with a thin, sharp spatula on one side, until you know that the sore is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if anything remains that cannot be scraped away, then open it with a thin, sharp instrument lightly, so that nothing is left behind;
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if pus emerges, dry the wound as necessary;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if they are malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize them until the pus is drained and all the corruption is removed; then drop honey or vinegar or wine on it.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the nose bleeds, and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healthy;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if moisture does not pass through as it should, know that there is corruption in the bone above, and so the instruments will not work to cut it out:
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	therefore you must insert a piece of thick linen thread, and it must be greased with lard, and there should be between each knot the width of a finger or less;
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and place one end of the thread in the patient's mouth at the tip of his tongue, and pull it through until it comes out the nose;
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many children do this at school, and it is an easy thing for anyone who wants to do it;
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold the head that comes from the nose in one hand, and the other head that comes from the mouth in the other hand, and pull them one after the other while being careful like those who are on a thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you know that the night has corrupted the flesh. Then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment before putting it back in the nose as before.
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of the flesh;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then put in the nose a plug of cotton for several days until it is healed. If medicine is needed to dry it out, then use it.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	And this is the shape of the instrument for purging the head, through which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And it can be of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp, like a candle, and lead them likewise;
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you see fit, make a closed candle, and fill the instrument with medicine to cleanse the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and have someone hold the head when heating the oil or any other liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart through the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times a disease arises in the brain called "tuberculosis", which grows and becomes large, until it is visible to the eye;
