et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and for this reason you must open it at the beginning, and cut out all that is rotten, then place on it the cautery or burning medicine;
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if one delays in opening it until it has grown large, then be careful that it is not hard, a bad colour, and lacking in feeling:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	nor touch it with iron for it is an encrusted abscess, for when one opens it, great harm comes to the patient;
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is from a soft touch, not a flowing colour, and you see that it can be completely covered, then empty the patient and cover it without fear, and treat the area with dry and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuation comes in one of these upper cartilage, it benefits little, unless in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	Therefore, whenever this happens to someone, look to see if the wound is fresh and bleeding;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then close the two lips with a stitch, then treat it until it heals;
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are separated on both sides, then you should cut all around their edges until they heal, then bring the two lips together with a stitch, and constrict them, and apply powdered dragon's blood over powdered incense;
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put a piece of strong plaster or other adhesive plaster over the powders, and leave it until it comes off by itself, then treat it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The manner of sewing is to prepare a solution:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	either with needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or with thread, as I have already made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	of lip abscesses
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	Within the lips there occur hard abscesses, resembling peas, both smaller and larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	therefore you should turn up the lips, and cut on each nodule, and take it with tweezers and scrape in each part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then apply vitriol powder to the wound after cutting, until the blood stops flowing;
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave it with honey, and clean the area of dried matter until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of gum swelling
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Often there grow on the gums a pustule that the old call 'albus';
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	you should grip it with tweezers and scrape at its root, and let the pus or blood flow out;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then place on the site vitriol powder, or other restraining and drying powders;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if the wound reopens after the incision, and this often happens, then close it again a second time, cauterizing it;
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not reopen after cauterization;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the forms of the fistulas to treat.
des sordens	from filth
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes they form at the root of teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and rough;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and sometimes the teeth turn black and green and rot, as the corruption spreads to the gums, and the teeth stink;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	you should make the patient hold his head in your hands, and press on the teeth or gums where they are visible, until nothing remains;
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and so you should do with blackness and greenness, and yellowing and other stains, until they are removed;ensí si tu vois que li dent est noir dedens et citrin, et la gencive citrine, et li dent puant et la gencive puant, tant qu’il n’i demore puanteur ne
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if one removes what is at its base, that is good.
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if not, then repeat it again the next day and the third day, until you have removed everything.
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that teeth have need of various instruments for removal, according to what the work shows them, because the forceps with which one removes the teeth are of a different shape from those used to remove things between the teeth.
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	And these shapes and others should be prepared for you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when you cure a tooth of its pain that you delay pulling it as long as you can, because it must not be done quickly.Et si li dent est en tel leu de sa dolor que on ne peut le traire, et qu’il soit de si grant dolor qu’on ne doit pas le
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	Because it is a very high substance until one has no excuse to pull it out.Et si li dent est en tel leu de sa dolor que on ne peut le traire, et qu’il soit de si grant dolor qu’on ne doit pas le raier, car c’est une substance
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the patient is forced to pull, you must be certain of the tooth socket.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and he believes it is in a sound tooth, and has the good tooth pulled;
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and yet the pain does not leave him thereby, as long as the bad tooth remains, for we have already tried this with those healers;
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are quite certain of the tooth that is aching, then you must scrape all around it with a spatulum and press hard to push back the gum on all sides;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then seize it with your fingers or with fine tongs at the gum line and wiggle it gently until it is well loosened, then grip it firmly with the tongs;
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and have the patient's head between your knees, and hold it steady so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	Then pull out the tooth carefully without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of those instruments and insert it into each side gently, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the tooth is broken and has a hole in it, then you must fill it with wax where the hole is;
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if he tightens it subtly with tweezers so that it does not break when being tightened;
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and one must work around the gum very gently to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful that you do not break it, and leave a part of it behind, and cause greater pain to the patient through the maliciousness of the root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And beware of doing as the ignorant surgeons do, who in their haste and arrogance sometimes break the jaw, and don't listen to what we have instructed.
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but sometimes cause great sickness by hurting the roots or breaking the jaw, as we have often seen.
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is loose, wash the gum with wine or garlic and salt;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, then apply crushed vitriol to the site;
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if that doesn't work, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The instruments for pulling teeth should have long, thin points and wide handles so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth;
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be made of thick metal so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be well-made iron, and they should be toothed to grip the roots.
de la racine des dens	of the tooth roots
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains in its place, you should apply wet cotton to the area for one or two days until the skin softens, and then use tweezers called "algefri" that make the shoulder look like a bird's beak.
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	They should be made inside as sharp as a file, and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tweezers, you must uncover the skin all around the root, and insert the instrument called "althali", that is, a spatula, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	It should be sturdy and thick so that it does not break, and if the root comes out through it, that' is good.
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	If not, use all your tools, and the forms come afterwards as follows:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one can also use this instrument with .ij. fingers, whose shape is as follows:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools which are in front of the reason for the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large tweezers, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let this tool be strong so that it does not break, and know that there are many tools for teeth.
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	There are also other tools which are not counted.
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And the wise master finds his own tools according to what his experience and the illness show him, for there are many types of illnesses that the ancients did not teach tools for due to their diversity; if he does not break through the bone or other bones but pierces through, then he should seek the tools that are needed as I have told you, and aid himself with gestures.
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And they must be thick and well-fitting to hold the bone, so that it does not slip, but can be held and removed;
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	then restore the place with appropriate medicine, and if there is swelling in the bone, and it is small, then treat it with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When a tooth appears not according to nature, and its shape is ugly, especially in virgin women, you must know whether the tooth is new after teething, and is not in the right place, and cannot be filed or ground down:
adonques lou raie;	then pull it out;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if there is an abscess with the tooth, take this instrument, of which the shape is like a small beak, and made of iron sharpened at its tip;
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And tap it gently day by day because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others. And if it is apparent that it can be ground down, then grind it with a file like this, in the shape shown:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	it is also like a file, with which needles are made;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and in lime gently pick at the tooth a little bit by bit, so that it does not move until it comes out;
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then smooth it at the end with no razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and it cuts the tongue, then file down the roughness until it is even so that it does not cut the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth is loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the front teeth are loose from either a blow or falling, and the patient cannot bite down on what they eat without it coming out, and you have tried restraining medicines without success,
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	then they should be restrained with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots away, but gold never moves.
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	The wire should be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the amount of space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you see the teeth leaning to one side, take a thread and tie it double between two healthy teeth, then place the head between the loose teeth, whether there is one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then start the binding again from where you began, and stretch your hand gently and firmly until it does not move;
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and tie it at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut the thread with pliers and gather it together, then tie it between the healthy teeth so that it does not irritate the tongue;
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	then leave it as tightly as possible for as long as it can stay in place, and if it comes undone or the thread breaks, tie it with another thread;
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	it will stay in place and serve its purpose for as long as needed, and this is the shape of the teeth and how they lean to one side, as you can see;
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when a tooth falls out, if one puts it back in its place, bit by bit, as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and no one who is not wise and experienced should meddle with it, and sometimes a tooth is made from cow bone, and it is put in the place where there is a gap, and it is held steady as we have said, and it remains and functions for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	cut off the hair of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Sometimes this type of growth comes from under the tongue, where nature creates it;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or as a result of an injury.
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the treatment is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and put his head in your lap, and lift up his tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then grab the nerve under the tongue, as wide as the tongue is dislocated from its socket, and if there is swelling or a lump, which is due to an injury, then push in with the fingernail and grab it under the tongue;
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and be careful that the split is not too deep, because of the artery underneath.
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	And when you have finished, raise the area with rose water and parsley, or cold water, then put underneath the tongue a tent made of linen;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and treat the patient every night so that the wound does not close over.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if there is bleeding, put ground glass onto the area;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the blood is flowing, cauterize it with a slow-acting cautery which is good for this purpose.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Then treat it again and again until it is healed;
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see it is black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is gangrene.
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	And if it is inclined to white pus and there is moisture, pierce it with an éléphant's tusk, and drain it from one side and the other;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if their blood flows onto your work, then place powdered vitriol on it until it is stained, then return to your work until you have finished everything.
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then lift the ax and the saw, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	from abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes, bumps called "godath" (possibly referring to a type of ulcer) appear in the throat, and they are properly called "almonds." When you treat them as described in the previous section and they do not heal, then be cautious:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	if it is a hard abscess of a small size and light color, do not touch it with iron.Si li corps est de la figure d’une bete fendee, et li corps est mort, il ne le puet demorer; mais si li
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if the body is shaped like a split animal, and the body is dead, it cannot survive. But if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron due to blood flow;Car il se doit curer en autre manier que li corps soit san: il doit curer en le
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but let it grow until it is long, and then you will cut it off, or it will break on its own.
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are of a white color and the roots are thin, then prepare the instrument for cauterizing, but first examine whether the abscesses have calmed down and become quiet.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then let the patient sit facing the sun, and his head in your lap, and open his mouth and hold the instrument between his teeth, and press his tongue down on it so that the tip of the instrument is positioned correctly.
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	It should be made of silver or thin brass like a small knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	When you have pressed the tongue against the tip of the instrument and seen the abscess, grab it with forceps and pull it out, as far as you can.
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and bring some cloth with you, then the cup to the instrument, from which is the shape, that looks like some strength;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	the ends are bent and one towards the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	If you do not have this instrument available, use tweezers, which should be shaped like a hook:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And they are serrated on one side and smooth on the other;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and when you have cupped one of the testicles, then cup the other in the same way, and after the incision gargle the patient with warm water, and water and garlic, and if there is bleeding, then gargle the patient with water, or pomegranate peels are cooked, or myrrh, and similar things, until the blood is stanched;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then he heals until it is healed;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	and sometimes other abscesses grow in the throat besides the two testicles, so cup them then as the two testicles are cupped.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman of an abscess which was inside her throat, that is to say, a small abscess.
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and had almost closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the passageway which was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if it continued for one or two more days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had become so swollen that it had pushed up two warts from the back of her throat.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I therefore acted quickly, and inserted a hook into the abscess, then pulled it outwards, and extracted a large amount of pus;
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then I made an incision in the other nostril, and cleared her throat and pressed on her tongue;
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	afterwards, I inserted a hook into the abscesses, and scooped out some of it, and only a little blood came out;
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and thus the passageway of the throat was cleared for the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to lance this abscess for a long time;
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscesses grew back again, filling the space that I had emptied, until it became very large;
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	so I lanced and cauterized it within the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	thus it stopped growing;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I left that area, and may God do with him what he will after I am gone.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the eye descends to the pupil, and it is swollen and distant, it is called "perpendicular";
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is below it is large and round, it is called  "eye".;
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is cut as we have said in the division, and the cautery does not help, and you see that the abscess has subsided and it is subtle, then you must scoop it out;
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and that which is round and gathered together and not distant;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is blood red or fawn colored or black, then you should avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have described, from its whiteness and length, you should have the patient sit facing the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument which we mentioned earlier:
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then insert the needle into the eye, and draw it out from underneath, and cut off the tip of one of the two instruments that I mentioned for the incision on the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And you should not cut deeper than the excess which is beyond the natural limit;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you cut deeper, it harms the voice and speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use what we said about the incision on the two almonds, and treat it until it heals.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of covering, then you should use an incision to treat his fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the method of cautery is for acute fever.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And let the patient place his head in your lap, and then press his tongue against the instrument we mentioned in the chapter on cauterization, and mix it with hot water, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and use the application of this instrument, whose shape is described as follows:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	At the end of the shaft there is a cup or bowl in which the medicine is placed, like the bowl of a spoon, and with the instrument one applies all the medicine to the eye;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient should lie on his side, so that the saliva and mucus run out of his mouth from the medicine, so that it does not descend into the throat and lungs;
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then hold your hand over the medicine and press it onto the eye for about half an hour, until you see it becoming soft and the stinging of the medicine subsiding;
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see [it], take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wet the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument all the way into the cotton on the cane above, so that the cotton sticks to the ulcer;
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then leave it to dry and fall off after 4 or 5 days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to renew the cautery with medicine, do so, and after the cautery is complete, wash around the ulcer with cotton dipped in butter, and cleanse what is around the medicine;
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then rinse with cold water, and treat with gargles until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than incision or cautery;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	If it is treated by fumigation according to this method, take calamintha and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and avens and similar herbs, and assemble them all or some of them in a pot, and put garlic in it, and let it boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pots are well glued with strong earth, and inside the pot there is a chewed instrument according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	It can be made of silver or bronze, and one end is placed in the mouth of the patient so that the vapors rise into the eye through the canal until the eye is numbed.
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	Afterwards, he repeats this often until the eye dries out. Be careful not to do this at the beginning of a hot abscess, for many things can happen then.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and not to do this except during the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, take a straw and put an egg yolk inside it so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot;
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	for the straw will not let the vapor harm the mouth, and this is a good and healthy treatment together.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times an object gets stuck in the throat, such as a fish bone or some other thing.
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	If you can see something in the throat, then press the tongue against it with your instrument under the light of the sun until you feel movement;
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and if something is stuck in the throat and cannot be removed, then you should make the patient vomit until the meat is cooked in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	by chance the object may come out through vomiting;s’il ne peut muer la chose tant qu’il soit cuite en l’estomac,
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	If the object cannot be moved while it is still in the stomach, or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of rope, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread;et li faice boire vin et aiglent;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and give him wine and vinegar to drink; and attach a string to the sponge and then swallow it;Et se li morcelz de pain sont trop gros, li faice les rem
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes to the surface, then it will bleed, and then you will pull it out;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come out as we have said, then take an instrument of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And the instrument should be curved at its tip so that it can more easily enter the throat, and the head should be lifted up high;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, or he will choke, nor push the bone inside;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and it is better that the patient himself inserts the instrument, so that he can feel where the object is;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	if he swallows it, then he should pull it out with the instrument evenly, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the saliva of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Sometimes the blood is drawn, as I have said in the division, through medical treatments;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and if this does not help, then look at the back of the throat towards the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument that I have told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, draw it out with a small hook, or with fine tweezers suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a pointed stick, and insert it into the throat of the ill person; then heat the tip of the stick with hot iron, and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has a fever all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take a full glass of cold water, open your mouth and pour it in without swallowing, moving the water around with your hand frequently.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and as soon as the blood feels the water, it will clot.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not clot as we have said, then smoke out the patient with assafetida using the instrument I mentioned for smoking out the throat.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Do this many times, because it will clot without bleeding.Et s’il se trouve en la bouche ou a la gorge lou sang qu’il ne peut engluitir,
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the method of smoking is that you heat a pot with burning charcoal until it has a layer of ash, and in this ash is the tip of the instrument;
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	then you shall apply the smoke, and the patient place the end of the cane in his mouth, and close his mouth so that the smoke does not escape but reaches the blood vessels.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the blood vessels will burst now, and if they do not, then resume the smoke treatment many times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and let the patient endure thirst, and eat salted and bitter things, and drink no water;
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then it will be necessary for her to go out by this method of treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument used to treat the blood vessels is, when one can see it, like bent tongs in order to enter the throat;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and has the appearance of a surgeon's forceps, and it has roughness from liming, so that what it grasps, it cannot let go;
et vez ci la forme:	and see here the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	There are many kinds of abscesses, according to what recollections come here after from both this book and others, and they differ in penetration and size:
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and they are of two types, the first of which is in its appearance the same, and due to what it holds in moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second kind is due to the locations where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundations, and the abscesses of fleshy places are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And one must not pierce abscesses until the boil is mature according to its completion;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and there are some that one must pierce when they have become crusty, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses that are near joints.Et sont divers les apostemes, car il en ont de lor taille et lor perforation;
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and one lets it be so long that it is pus around, perhaps the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.Et si il le percierent, et il se curast adés, si est cause de grant mal a celui qui a la jointure, car il ne puet remuer li meisme membre tant qu’il vult.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Abscesses are diverse, for they have different sizes and penetrations. The abscess may be near the principal member, and if you delay the penetration until it is mature, it will harm the principal member;
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	or if it is near the foundation, one must pierce it so that it dies.
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and one must not pierce an abscess without digestion being complete, except for the one that is near the foundation, which should be allowed to drain freely inside, and a fistula will result.
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and it cannot heal in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And one must know the hour of the piercing of the abscess which is dead according to completion, and it is when the pain is eased, and the lessening of fever, and the decrease in swelling and redness, and the cooling and hardening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and one must pierce in the highest part of the abscess, and where it appears softest;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and the piercing must be done deeply into the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints, near nerves, and throughout all places where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	For those who bend, according to the affected member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to let the piercing wait until it is confirmed with digestion complete, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce it before this, then the body is stretched out from its venom, and it is filled with much filth.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and perhaps harden his lips and his depths.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is an abscess which has been pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And you should treat it with small abscesses, small holes;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large holes, and many slits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if there are such abscesses where one must cut into the brain, and cover;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it has become as soft as a grape, and is dead, then one should do as one does with blisters:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and some are split into three angles, and some are covered as the fuel of myrrh, as with abscesses of the bones;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and some where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who have no head, as with a superficial abscess, you must pierce it directly.
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	And when the abscess is large and has formed a great boil, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus in one hour, but only a portion of it.
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	Then pack the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more the following day;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	Do this repeatedly, a little at a time, until all the pus has been released.
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Especially if the patient is weak, or a woman carrying a child, a small child, or an elderly person.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For sometimes an experienced surgeon jumps with the release of gas from the belly, which may kill the patient, and you would not know it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore, be very cautious with this chapter. After you have pierced the abscess, wash the wound and check if the wound of the abscess is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it's a clean cut, apply bandages made of linen or old cotton;
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess with many openings, you should put a tent in each opening so that they come together.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have cut into the abscess and cut around it, then you should fill it with old cotton or a lining of linen without moisture, and ligate it up to the third day.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then remove the bone and treat the wound with ointment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, bring cold water and vinegar, and moisten the cloth, and place it over the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the blood flow continues, and there is administration of medicine and treatment, and the powders I have described earlier in this book, and it occurs in winter, and the abscess is very nervous, then you should put wet tents and clothes soaked in hot wine and oil on top.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in the summer, and the area is fleshy, then you should put wet clothes soaked in water and oil or cold wine and oil on top for up to a third of a day, as we have said.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then open the abscess, clean and treat it as necessary until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this is what one should generally understand about the treatment of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	I have told you how to proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and now listen to the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	From the neck come small abscesses, which are common in people who work in wool, like the pimples on a goat's udder; there are many variations of these.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some that are fatty and others that contain pus and moisture;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and there are some which are hard and stone-like in texture, and they do not cause doubt if the artery does not oppose them.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the operations of the waist are such that you should test all instruments called "dislocators", from which the forms come later, what they contain.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they will push it out from above the length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is evacuated, one should scorch it without leaving anything behind that holds the moisture, for it will return as soon as something is left behind.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is available;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound and let it sit until the next day.
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and those who are delayed by night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then resume the cotton, as before, on the second and third days, until you know that it no longer remains overnight;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wound with ointment appropriately, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess contains pus, then open it according to this method, from the long side;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and cut your fingernails, and remove all scabs, and put all your efforts into milking the wound where it lies under the skin;
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the artery opposes you, then do what I told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also treat an abscess if it is piercing, and cutting and treating as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cut on the piercing abscess and moistness is lighter, because they are full of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And in some of these abscesses, if there is no moisture, and among them was one that I opened on the head of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and I found the abscess like a hard stone, rough and white, and could not be broken;
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if one were to cut them, they would bleed just as much as a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses that come on the head or neck, as opposed to those which come on the heads of children and at the roots of ears, the opening should be left open in the most dependent part to allow pus to drain out.
et les cure si com il covient.	and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times abscesses occur on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin area, and sometimes they come elsewhere in the body, and they are large, and some are joined together.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scrofula is properly within its coat, like the nodule and abscess of the neck, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and there are many similarities among them.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and others that are stubborn and do not want to heal.And li chiés des enfans si adont qu’il ont scrophule dedens le col, ou dedens la teste, ou dedens les oreilles, ou dedens les costes, et il n’i a pas de scrophule qui ne contienent moistor et sanguine.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	Therefore, if you see one of good disposition to touch, and resembling the color of the body, and soft in each part and not hard on the nerves of the neck or artery or channel, and not deep;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	you should cut it from above and scrape off the skin of each part, and if you have need, cut the two lips of the ulcer at the edges, as we have said about abscesses on the neck;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and pull it little by little, being careful not to touch the nerve or the vein, and do not use the spatula or forceps, so that the hand does not slip, and do not look too far ahead, so that you do not cover what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you touch the vein or artery and it will not let you work, put into the wound powdered vitriol, or any powder that stops bleeding, and bind the wound.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and leave it until the abscess is relieved and the wound is softened and begins to suppurate.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the bleeding has stopped, return to your work, until you have finished it.
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	Then examine with your finger if there are any small scrofulae remaining; cut them out and clean them.Et si tu copes a la voinne ou artere, et ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, you should not cut that scrofula at its root, but ligature it with a strong double thread and let it drop down from it without harm.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then employ the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you pick the entire scab, you should bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now, so that no superfluity remains due to the size of the scab.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	you should attend to picking at its root, and pulling it out, and sewing it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrofula that have suppuration, pierce where it appears to be flowing;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	And piercing it thus as the one before mentioned, depending on it, then treat it with tenting with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption;
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the wound is well cleaned, then cure it with ointment bandaging, until it is healed.Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double
de squinance	of scrofula
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients said and spoke about the incision of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	But I have never seen anyone in our land who does this, and it is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those with a squint, the flap of skin in the throat called the "epiglottis" must be cut away;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and this is not helped by that, because all the veins and the pus from the malady are in those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the lungs, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, we should cut it under the third or fourth rib, a small slit across, between the two circles, or according to the quantity of the slit in the soft palate; not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those places are suitable for the cut of the epiglottis where there is no cartilage, and the vessels are long from there.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is fearful, then he should stretch the skin of the throat all the way to the Adam's apple, then split the chest until it reaches the backbone.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid blood vessels, if you see any, and then cut through the windpipe, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the flow of blood from the wound in the backbone, and by the lack of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed at which one doubts about strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound in the chest, and stitch it up completely without the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer remedies that promote flesh growth, until it is healed.And if there is any sign of gangrene in the wounded man, cut off all the dead tissue with a sharp knife and apply an ointment
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is completely healed, and the patient is judged dead, and the lack of breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore, cut through the epiglottis so that the patient cannot choke, and he will breathe through the wound, and thus be saved from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and therefore the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease had passed, and it passed in three or four days. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and treat it, until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a lady take a knife and stab herself in the throat, cutting some of the windpipe;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to heal her, and found her as good as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found that the blood had not come out through the throat or windpipe but instead was escaping through the wound itself.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, sewed up the wound, and treated it until it healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and the lady had no more than a hoarseness in her voice, and she returned to her senses afterwards;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	therefore I say that one should have no fear of cutting into the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This hernia is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a large hernia in the color of ochre, and it is very common in women.
et est selonc II manieres:	And there are two ways of treating it:
naturez, et accidens;	Natural and accidental;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Or natural without cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental ones are in two ways, one which is similar to fat and the other like an abscess that comes from an artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And there is fear in it, and one should not operate with force unless the hernia is small; you should test and probe throughout the whole opening:
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it as soft as fat and there is no vein, then treat it like an abscess and cut all around its head if there is nothing there. But if:
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	You probe well and treat the abscess as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways to do this, and I will describe all their appearances.
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And now I must explain the difference between a cut and a dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that a dislocation is when there is a constant fever until the swelling has passed and the wound has healed:
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	then the fever and heat abate.Et la fievre et le chalor reposiez, si comence li porriture, qui
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With a cut, there is no fever or heat or pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is the color of the body's flesh. It starts like a pimple and becomes swollen:et si li porriture ne voudra point acomplir, si la fievre et le chalor ne ceient point, et li porriture ne creissez point;
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and if the swelling won't go down and the fever and heat don't abate, and the pus doesn't increase in size, then they are of two types: dry or moist, and their colors vary as I have described.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the treatment of the nose, you should first test and examine it with an instrument called an "introducer", according to what its shape comes from in the following chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring into abscesses on the brain is to squeeze the most moist place that you find in the abscess, and gradually move your fingers, until you feel that the instrument has penetrated the core, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then pull out the instrument, and be careful not to let anything slip out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the pus flows easily, whatever its color, treat it as I have said for other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the instrument no pus comes out, know that it is hard, so treat it in the shape of a cross, and grab it with tweezers, and gently scrape each side and guard the membrane where it lies so that you draw it out healthy with the brain.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot draw it out healthy, then pull it in pieces so that nothing remains.Et est-il grant danger que li chiés de l’ajutoire soit desaloiez, et il ne peuit demorer en son leu; et il est grant dolor al
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if he does not move anything, then it returns to him many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if he stays a little while and the wound does not trouble him, then apply some corrosive powders to the wound, press on it, and put hot poultices on it; treat the wound with other treatments until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the wound is large, then cut the two lips of the wound and treat it with what heals flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the bleeding vein is contrary to you or another, then hurry and apply powdered vitriol to the spot and leave it there for two or three days until the wound scabs over and the bleeding stops;
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to binding what has been left open.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	Here are the forms of instruments for dislocation, and there are three types:
grans et moien et petit;	large, medium, and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three types of warts which are called "albaret", and one type is called "breb", and there are three varieties:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, medium, and small, in order to surround the abscesses of fistulas;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are like the needles used to sew witches, made of brass, iron, or silver, and the yellow-tinted ones are the most effective, proven to be so, for surrounding the growths of fistulas;
et sont de III manieres:	and there are three types:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the opening of the fistula.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of the knives are very varied, as you can see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	large, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and there are knives with two curves of three types as well;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if [it is] the elbow which has three curves, and [is] also in three ways;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if [it is] the elbow which has two curves, and [the] elbow of one curve only, and  [is] in three ways;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The heads of these knives are cutting tools, and there are some which do not cut except from one side, so that we do not cut the vein or nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and these probes are placed in handles, so that the patient does not hurt themselves when opening abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three types:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	large, small and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and we do not use them except in fleshy places, such as legs and arms, and breasts, and armpits, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes another small instrument is made, resembling the slices of a fig, according to this shape, with which one stanches blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is sometimes placed in the place that heals by filling the veins and arteries, and sometimes they are filled according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell up when they become corrupt, so that they look like women's breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, should apply the ointment described in this chapter from line b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with an ointment made from pitch, then stitch together the two lips of the wound, and let it heal.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	And if the breast sags down, and becomes soft due to its size just like it happens to women, then they should make two cuts above it, like two similar incisions;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	and the two cuts should meet at the bottom, so that the larger cut contains the smaller one according to this shape from line b to g;
