et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	And when you have finished milking, put on the wound wool soaked in wine and rose oil;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it twistedly, but do not kick it;
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and milk it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one kicks the vein is curved, and it does not cut, so that it does not open the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of a thick curvature because if it were thin, it would pierce the vein but let it be thick as we have said and here is the form.
de la voinne civile	of a civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in legs, in hot parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry land where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and by chance it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens with warts that grow underneath the skin, just as snakes and worms do, growing between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	If the signs of the beginning of this wound are that a great inflammation comes in the leg, then the location changes, and the wound begins to come out, just as a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the shoulder opens, you must wrap around it a piece of plaster three and a half inches to four inches wide, and tie it, leaving the plaster hanging down on the leg, and every time it dislocates, wrap it around the plaster and the wound.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and wrap around the remaining plaster, but do not cover its root at all until it is completely healed.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it will enter the flesh and cause an abscess and pus in that spot, and a serious illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Because of this, it should be treated little by little until the very end, so that nothing remains in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	And sometimes this vein, when treated from the palm of the hand, is ten or twenty inches long, and a man came to me once whose was twenty inches long. And when you cut it, it causes a stream or gush, and pierces right through to the bottom so that everything flows out.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And the matter inside is emptied, and medicine-impregnated dressings are applied for a few days to cause pus to form, then it is treated like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And sometimes this vein has many branches, especially when it opens at the joints of the foot or ankle, and there are many gushes, and from them springs blood.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that live between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called "cattle disease" in our land, because it often affects oxen. It is caused by a small worm that lives between the skin and flesh, moving throughout the body, ascending and descending, until it bursts through the skin where it goes, and escapes.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	It is also accompanied by the emergence of humors, like worms, serpants, roundworms, and other parasites in the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	Its malice is feared because when it moves through the body and reaches the head, it can enter and destroy the eye.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	This happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it moving and wriggling, one cannot help but feel revulsion.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	Therefore, you must tie the area above and below tightly with a strong string, then cut it out and if the worm is deep in the flesh and you cannot extract it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greater harm he does, as we have said, is that he runs to the eye.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the eye, grab under his chin firmly, then lift up and pull out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and one must use the treatment for purifying the body with dissolveing medicines to remove bad humors and to guard against constipating foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called "vomiting" in our language, and it is a pain that comes to various limbs and then moves from limb to limb;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and soon after, I saw it rise to her shoulder as fast as anything, as quick as silver when it moves from place to place. It moved rapidly and looked like a worm. ;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain leaves that spot, and goes to the shoulder, and then a little later runs through the whole body, until it reaches the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she began to turn around the body, just as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very surprised how it moved from limb to limb like that, because I had never seen this disease progress in that way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Nevertheless, I have seen many whose pain has moved from one place to another, but I have not seen it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought that it was because women's bodies are dry and their veins uncovered, and that this caused the wind to be constrained in them;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and they do not appear according to this reason in those who are constipated, and who have moist bodies and relaxed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see this disease being cured, and the patient feels the pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then open up above and below, and then press gently until the wind is forced out of its place;
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the area;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it yourself, then have the person who performs enemas, as with foul-smelling pills, and serapium pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the part of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of their appearance is such that some have large points, some small, some sharp, and some smooth;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some have two angles, and some have tongues, and some have pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and those that break in a member do so in two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in a principal member it breaks, as with brain, heart, liver, lung, kidney, intestines, bladder, and similar members.Or il chiet en membre de la chair, si com en osse, en tendins, en ligamenz, en nervoz, en veines, en arteries, et en toute l’autre chair qui
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it therefore breaks in any of these members, and the signs of death that I will tell you about appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	Then you must be wary of extracting this arrow, for death often follows such a course;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And if this evil sign is not apparent to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain is when the arrow pierces and penetrates the bone, and the syphilis emerges from above the brain, and there is scotomata, and an odor, and a discharge, and redness, and inflammation of the tongue, and spasms, and a disturbance of the mind, and vomiting of blood;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps it emerges from the nose or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps they lose their speech and voice;et li sains lours le corps et li membres et le vis,
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and the healthy person feels pain in the body and members and face, and from the wound emerges white moisture resembling pus, and also like a bruise on meat;et si li sains se levent, il die qu’il a grant mal, et si li saige bevet,
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears, keep to the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of an arrow wound when it hits the body are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in a hard object, not hollow;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and sometimes the arrow wound goes silent like the pulse, and there is dark blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and syncope:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then know without a doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that never leaves the lung is that without pain foam comes from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow hits the bottom of the foot, it is between the small bones;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and there is great pain and deep sighing;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and all the limbs move from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow hits the stomach, perhaps something undigested will jump out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow hits the belly, and nothing comes out of the bowel but feces, then there is no hope for a cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow hits the bladder, and the urine comes out in a spray and there is leakage, and the patient feels great pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and armpit and spine of the back and hip and thigh and leg, and similar limbs, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery and is not venomous, as I will tell you so that you can do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	There was a man who got an arrow in his eye socket at the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I probed it and pulled it out from under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without a scar.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And I pulled out an arrow that had pierced the fatty tissue under his eye and was lodged beneath the eyelid; the arrow was stuck with its tip pointing towards the bridge of the nose, and it was as long as a Turkish archer's arrow, with a thin shaft and no feathered fletching. It had pierced through without any sign of blood or pus.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The patient healed without any complications.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	I pulled an arrow out of the throat of a Christian man; it was an Arabic arrow with feathered fletching:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I cut away the barbs and carefully extracted it, and the Christian man healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And brought a arrow to a man who had it lodged in his chest or belly, and thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after thirty days had passed, his condition did not improve;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, and extracted it, and he had no bad reaction.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man who has an arrow lodged in his back, and the wound is sutured over;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remains inside him, and his natural functions do not change, nor does he experience any discomfort in any of his natural processes.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And you see another man who has an arrow lodged in his face, and the wound is sutured over;Et demora li saiette lor dedens, si com je vos di, et ne fu nulz dous de ses oevres naturels changiez
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	And the arrow remains inside them, as I have told you, and none of their natural functions are changed, and they remain without
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many others.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And there was a certain arrow shot at the king, a prince of the realm, that had pierced his eye and was slightly inclined towards the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was fully embedded.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to attend to him after three days had passed.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I examined it carefully and couldn't feel anything;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	but he felt a piercing pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the point of the arrow. I applied a soothing and digestive poultice to the area to reduce swelling;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the head of the arrow. Je mis sus lo leu de la saiette poudre de fer et de plomb, et
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied powder of iron and lead to the head of the arrow, and reapplied the poultice daily. The wound healed, but the patient felt the presence of the arrow in his eye for a long time;
et il le me dist.	and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I put corrosive medicine on the wound for several days until it was open and I probed it and felt the head of the arrow which was embedded there.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I applied this medicine to the wound until the head of the arrow became visible;
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and it healed well within four months. Then I enlarged the wound with forceps and could not extract the arrow;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	so I continued to manipulate it with instruments until one day, according to what is written in this chapter, I drew it out and healed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And those who have knowledge of such things judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	so I restored it and the wound was healed completely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Here I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your care on what I do not say, for books cannot include everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but the wise masters compare on very little great things, and on what they are present and lacking, they find new works and new tools, to the descent of strange things that come in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows grow in the members where they are stuck according to two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the place where they enter, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which goes out through where it entered is an arrow entering into their muscles, and sometimes goes out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not go out now, then leave it so that the flesh around it becomes rotten and the outlet is relieved;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, then leave it like that for a few days, and move it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it leaps, and if it does not leap, then pierce all around with a very thin stick until the orifice widens, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head, and penetrates one of the brain's ventricles, and some of the aforesaid accidents manifest in the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	do not pull it out, but leave it as long as several days, for if the arrow reaches the brain, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone and does not reach the brain, and the patient remains for several days without any bad symptoms, then treat it by extraction.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is lodged very deeply and cannot be removed, then administer cauterization around it, as I have told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the wound until it is closed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow has been driven into the body so that it cannot be seen, then look for it throughout the body;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then draw it to a suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then open it as widely as the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if there are barbs on the arrow that hold it in place, then cut away the flesh where the barbs are located on both sides as far as you can, and then bend or twist the barbs of the arrow so that you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful not to break the arrow as you pull it out more forcefully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot remove it in one go, then leave it until the flesh around it is swollen, and then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood causes a problem, then refer to what we have said about curing in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of cutting into a nerve and opening a vein, and use every trick you know to pull out the arrow safely, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and place the patient in the same position as when the arrow struck him, for that is the best help you can provide; and if you cannot do this, then place him according to the signs that show themselves.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another direction, or where something of it appears, or the skin is swollen in that spot where one can see or feel it clearly:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	cut above it, as high as the tweezers can reach, and then pull it out:
si saut fuer maintenant.	if it jumps out immediately.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is caught in the bone, then rotate your hand rapidly, so that it goes into the bone and widens the opening, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then leave it and try pulling again until it comes out:et s’il est en haut ou en bas, et ne peut demourer en son lieu, et tu vois que il se remue, si le mets sus li foyez selonc le membre qu’il a la dis
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if it is high up or low down, and cannot stay in its place, and you see that it is moving, then reset the joint according to the limb that is affected by the dislocation:and if there is an
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if it is cut, and you see to administer bandaging, then let him administer the instrument chewed, so that the tip of the arrow enters the gum of the instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then bite down, and if the arrow is chewed, let him bite down on the instrument with its tip entering in, to aid extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow has touched, then you must cut all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then cure the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow is cut or pierced in the mouth, belly, bladder, or side, and it is close by, and you can cover it up, then let him cover it up.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And be careful to not cover the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then close the wound, if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of tweezers used to treat arrows are similar to an owl's beak, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	There are many ways of doing this:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is like that of a bird's feather, to push against the tip of the arrow, just as it is shaped:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of tweezers to pull and to check if it is there:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common body veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	Of veins from which one heals there are 31, of which there are 16 in the head, namely:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	II. Veins that are behind the ears, called "two herbech
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the II arteries that are in II temples apparent;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the eyelids, which are called "aspirations".
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is in the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the top of the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two windpipes which are in the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are above the lips, and these are the veins called "augerich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins which are commonly used for bleeding are five in each arm:the first vein is called  "superficial external", and it runs along the arm just below the skin, from
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the  "cephalica", which is on the left side of the chest, and common people call it the  "vein of the head";the second vein is called   "superficial internal", and it runs along the arm towards the palm, from
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the middle one is called    "fast", and it is composed of the   "cephalica" and the   "basillica", and common people call it the   "vein of the heart";the third vein is called    "basillica", and it runs along the arm towards the back of the hand, from
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic vein is located on the right side, and the lay people call it "wound of the belly", and it is situated above the bladder, and it is that one which opens clearly above the scrotum.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the salvatoria vein is the one between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches:
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and in the foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is below the curve of the scrotum on the left side, and the second one is at the ankle on the right side;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein called "nest", which is at the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding from the veins that are behind the ears helps with old cataracts and with emigrine;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the qualities of the surgeon, as I told you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then tighten the patient's neck with a rope, so that the two veins appear behind the ears, descending from the head;
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	hold it tightly at your waist, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, press inwards;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lance and pierce under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein upwards, and cut both the skin and the vein well twice with the lance, and let blood flow until you see it;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then tighten and bind it, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The healing of the two arteries that are in the two temples, it helps with old-age blindness and habituated dim vision, and to the body of the eyes, watery eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the healing agent are as I said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and that the patient holds his neck still, so that the two veins are clearly visible;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pain in your chest, and then signs inwardly;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then lightly press the vein near the top of your index finger, and insert the lance below, and press the vein upwards, and draw out the blood according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on top;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then let it heal, and leave it until it is healed;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have spoken of their formation and extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The sores of the frontal vein are as valuable as the cephalic veins in old diseases of the face, and in emigration and redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its qualities are such that the patient twists his neck so that the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "digging", of which this is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let the blood issue according to the amount you want;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then loosen the neck of the patient, and ligate the vein so that it is healthy, sometimes with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	Nevertheless, the flames should not be too narrow;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and he should heal crosswise, because the bone is close, and might break the flame when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healing of the two veins that are in the two eyelids, and also for eye-inflammation, redness, and diseases of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the nature of their healing is that the patient should twist his neck in some way, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then it heals, and the healing is through the tissue, a little way down from the long flame, a little wide, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps they will break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	Then make it bleed until you have enough blood, and then tie it up with a thread, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The healing of the vein in the nose is useful for nosebleeds and for sudden madness, and for diseases of the face, such as inflammation and redness that come to the face, and especially when it is chronic.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the quality of bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck, then pulls his nose to your left hand, and takes the subtle flame long, and inserts it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well there, and the blood will now begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then ligature it for a night, because it is quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	Bleeding from the two sinuses helps with strangulation of the windpipe, and at the beginning of hoarseness, and many illnesses, and impetigo, and scrofula, and herpes, and stomachaches;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck from both sides, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and the master is standing above the patient's head, and the patient is sitting on a chair, then cut the vein in the arm generously, then draw blood moderately, as needed.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then tie off the other vein, then gently constrict the veins, so that the patient is not strangled.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and let it be until morning, so that the wound can heal.
de la sainie des leivres	of bleeding from the gums
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of the veins in the lips helps with sores in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and splitting of the lips, and pain in the teeth and gums.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the bleeding is to have the patient sit in front of you, and constrict his neck as I've said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the lip, and examine both veins, one on the right side and the other on the left; you can identify them because they are black, and because there are small black veins around them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Cut both of them, and if you don't recognize them, and you're in doubt, then cut the largest one on each side, and likewise do the same for the veins above and below, as it's the same procedure.Et li voinnes qu’a l’enfre, si les cope a la fin, car il y a en l’enfre pluseurs veines que ont poeur;
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The bleeding of the veins that are under the tongue is helped by the bleeding of the cephalic vein, and it is in the constriction of the throat, and in the diseases of the eye, and in the diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the bleeder are that the patient should hold their hands out in front of the sun, and stick out their tongue, and look down on each side for a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	so therefore bleed both, but do not go too deep, for under them are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the neck from which one commonly bleeds are bled in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either with a large mirtin needle, or a thin olive-wood one as sharp as a needle, and it is called 'anesil';
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are large and thin according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame of myrtle is highly renowned, and it is wide as you can see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the veins smooth and full of clear blood, and those that contain thick and troubled blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and that is the shape of an olive-shaped flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed and subtle, used for bleeding veins that are fine and contain subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps diseases that are under the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the bleeding to be stopped, and for the artery underneath to be cauterized.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he opens the artery, and a gushing of blood comes, then it must be stopped, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and the flame should not be gripped, but cut as if with a knife.And if the artery bleeds, and gushing blood comes, then it must be stopped, as I have said; and the flame should not
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilic does not open clearly, then you must dislocate it, and change to another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you want some of them, or you heal in place of them the vein inside the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the cautery flame extinguishes, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to find the site of the bleeding, you must therefore stretch out the arm, and touch the site until you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the site with a cut, then tie up the arm, and cauterize the vein until the flame goes out;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and be careful not to pierce the artery when you see the site swell, for that is the artery;
eschui la donques.	avoid it therefore.Car si tu le feris en l’artere,
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it gush out high like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	therefore hurry, and put your finger on it for a long time, then take your finger off if the wound stops bleeding, as often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	bind up his arm and leave it, and do not move him who is sick.
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let him be afraid, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the wound is not clotting and he is bleeding profusely while you are waiting for the medicine, then press hard on the artery until it stops.
et estainche li sans.	and stop the flow of blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a piece of fir wood and split it, then take one half and tie it firmly in place until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	If the wound is clotting, that's good;si li sans ne estainchie, querre une escorce d’alier
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, get a piece of alder wood and, as we said earlier, use powders to stop bleeding.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the bandages are not wrapped in various positions because of the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The bleeding of the vein in the middle helps that it draws blood from the head above and the body below, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and the surgeon must be careful not to pierce too deeply and find the nerve, and it should swell and the wound be harmed, and perhaps it cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve opens in many people, but if it does not open in some because of its subtlety, then you must anoint it with the anesthetic;
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and avoid the nerve as much as you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if it has a vein between the two nerves, they cut it open.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The bleeding of the cephalic vein helps draw blood from the head and aids the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and one must open the vein with a flame from an olive branch or a myrtle twig, for it is the safest of all veins, since there are no nerves or arteries underneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nevertheless, one must find the lightest vein, and if one misses the first time, one should try again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and sometimes veins swell up in certain people, when one misses the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding depends on your thought process.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you should know about opening veins is that it is not done merely to treat disease but also to prevent it from coming;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and it can be performed in one of three veins that are in the arm:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	namely, the cephalic, the fast, and the basilic;li cephalique est li plus legiers de sainier, car il n’a pas
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should open the vein at the beginning of spring, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of digestion are apparent;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one must bleed him the first day or third, after two hours or three of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding which is administered to the sick has no fixed time, but when there is need, day or night, at all times and at all hours.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and one must not bleed children until they are fourteen years old, nor women carrying a fetus beyond the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the very elderly who have passed 60 years be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when someone wants to be bled, in whatever way, he should first clean out the intestines with a gentle enema if he has retained a lot of feces so that the veins do not draw harmful excess fluids from the intestines into the principal limbs.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Nor should one bleed those who are too bloated with food, nor those who are drunk, as long as it lasts, nor the hydropic.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if one is sick after colic, vomiting, diarrhea, and excessive sexual intercourse with a woman, from exertion, from lack of sleep or fasting, and from all that depletes the body through arms or the body itself.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then secretly restore the humor if it is thin, through food and drink and medicine if you have the power to do so.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then enter the bath if nothing else is helping, to restore the humor and to heal the wound around the navel, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and avoid hard work, straining, and excess during that day, and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be calm and cheerful, and let the patient be higher than the person healing them, and rub their arm 2 or 3 times, then tighten the bandage above the wound gently, for if it is too tight or too loose, it cannot heal the wound.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then he rubs the area with his hands, until the veins swell, and they are felt;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then moisten the needle with a little old oil, then place his finger from his left hand on that vein underneath the site he wants to cauterize, so that the vein does not burst and break when cauterized.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flow like cords when cauterized, and others that are full of wind and so when the needle is placed on them and the cautery is applied, they draw back from the heat and cannot be opened, and thus one must be careful of these.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if he opens the vein, and the wound is too narrow, then one must be careful with this.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens on the first attempt, that is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If not, then begin again a little lower down, or above the wound, if the swelling has subsided.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the swelling persists and the patient is in fear, then leave it for a day or two, and do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	Perhaps hot abscesses will form;
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not enter into a bath, then begin the bleeding again if she wishes;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the wound is small, or the blood flows slowly and you doubt that enough blood will come out, then insert the fleam directly into the wound;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and work a little gently, so that the swelling does not subside;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for it often happens, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the area swelling, do not begin the bleeding again, and place some linseed oil on it, for it lightens the body of blood, and is useful in that place where there is oil;
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and so administer the leech oil on each wound that you heal the veins to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and the same thing happens with triacle and bowels when they are placed in the wound;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	if subtly the blood splits and escapes when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if a large abscess comes, which often happens, especially when it is not healed in the first place or when the opening of the vein is small, you should hurry and put a damp sponge in lukewarm water on the wound, and hold it there for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and you should do this after the blood flow from the wound stops, and if it remains in place for several days with some blackness or green, then it does no harm;Et s’il vient a la voix qu’il se remue ou qu’il se fende, si le faict mal.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see it, put on something made of aloe or myrrh mixed with medicinal juice, a poultice, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often there is an abscess and an appearance at the base of the penis:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	then put your hand on it, and if you find the area soft to the touch, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Therefore, avoid putting anything we have mentioned on it, because sometimes it comes from an artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but let him dry-foment the area to harden it, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to its quantity and the strength of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it becomes red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it thick, let it go until it is thinned out;
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for one who is full and bloated, and needs bloodletting, that they make him a larger wound, and let the flames be wide;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and they should bleed him little and often, and they must bleed him by cutting across, not by pricking;
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this method of bleeding is safe from blood loss and nerve damage, and is better than bleeding from the long or wide vein.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for one whose body needs bleeding, it is necessary to give them moist bread in pomegranate juice;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If he is hot-tempered, let him eat moist bread with pomegranate juice three or four times before bleeding. And if he is of a cold complexion, let him eat moist bread with syrup of rosewater, or with scented honey syrup mixed with spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger and cardamom, and with fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during bleeding, after losing a lot of blood, then he should drink warm broth and fragrant syrup, and use other things that we have mentioned in the chapter on syncope, for opening the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to empty his arm and bleed again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by a large bleed, that he bleeds little by little according to the amount of his continued strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to open their arm after the first bleeding, and they have a strong body, then heal for .7 hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to bleed elsewhere, then they should bleed on the second day or the third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For there is much blood within the body which has become heated, and brings on fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	if one must draw out a great quantity, and widen the opening as far as it will stretch with the finger;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then you must examine all the conditions of healing, and put your hand on his pulse as he heals, so that death does not come to the place of the wound, and this often happens when the surgeon is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and one must not, when you see to unbind the arm and make the blood issue out a second time, and the opening is closed, press directly on it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is crooked, that he extends his arm suddenly, for that would be bad;sies qu’en la seconde saingniee tu leuisses li bras pendre par un drape, et li pertus soit sus loing de
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	letting the arm hang by a cloth, and the opening be distant from the shoulder; but let it be until it heals the second time;et
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you point the flame to the tip of the vein until the frozen blood in the vein melts and flows out, then place a little salt mixed with water on it, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not constrict it, until the abscess is reduced.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to let blood a second time, then bleed in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are healthy in the area of the vein in the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the way of bleeding is for the patient to put his hand in hot water until the vein is dilated;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then let him be bound up gently so that the vein appears well, then he should be bled from the middle, neither from the top nor the bottom;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and the cut should be wide, and bleeding should be done close to the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot come out, then put the hand back in hot water and let the blood run into the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is winter, do not put the hand back in hot water, for one puts their hand in warmer water in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the bleeding from this vein is safer than from any other vein, for there are neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The bleeding to save the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it is done:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Hold the hand, and put in warm water, until the vein is swollen, as one sees it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if it bleeds across, and you tie it from all sides, it will not hurt anything;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not go in too deep, for the nerves are stripped of flesh everywhere underneath, and then put the hand back in warm water if the blood is frozen in the wound, and it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have stopped the bleeding as much as necessary, then put oil and silk on the wound to heal quickly, and do this for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding in the left hand is beneficial for the disease of the mouse, and do everything just as I told you about the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve of the sophia is good for all diseases that are under the body, such as diseases of the stomach, and retention of fluids, and diseases of the kidneys, and the buttocks and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the qualities of its bleeding are such that the patient puts his foot in warm water, and rubs on the vein until it bursts, and he applies a poultice to the joint of the foot;
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot they go very fast.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	treat it then with the broadest vein, or at the ankle, which is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you treat it above the foot, beware of the nerves underneath, and treat it across as well by cutting.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the fire be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water, and let the vein bleed well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if it lacks the first time, do it again a little higher up, for the vein is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and thus do the same with the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The location of the sciatic vein is at the ankle bone, and its pulsation extends to the pain in the hip, when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And its quality is that the patient goes into the bath, and pulls up above the ankle three times by twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, then treat it in all ways you can, and across;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And it is better to cut it off because the skin is safe, and it is very relieved by hand.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not believe this, cut a vein in the leg that opens towards the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	Let the blood flow as you wish, then loosen the bandage and put on cotton and tighten it;
ele est maintenant sanee.	It is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	Of cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Cupping glasses are made from horn, or brass, or glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	And ventilation is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Either by cutting and drawing blood, or without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this ventilation which is without cutting, is according to two methods:ou par entremise de plave de vairre, ou d’arain;
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	Or it is through a glass plate, or brass; either it is with fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and ventilation which is done by hitting and by bloodletting if it is done in XIV places of the body, one of which is all at the top of the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and others are among the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others on each side of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the ventouse under the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the ventouse on both shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the ventouse above the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the ventouses among the two arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the ventouses on both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the ventouses on the two ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and ventilation does not draw blood, except from small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and because of this it doesn't weaken him at all, as with bloodletting from a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it must not be administered, neither by all fire nor by any heat, in any illness that comes from fullness, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if through necessity or habit it is necessary to bleed, then we should do so every hour at the beginning of the month, or at its end, and at intervals throughout each season.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	this is because there are some who have a heavy head when they need to bleed;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and some experience bloating and redness in their face, head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and some have a drop of blood in their mouth, and their tongue swells, and they bleed;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are some who dream, and see through the night blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially if it occurs during the night, we instruct them to drink a medicine after three hours.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	Bleeding from the nose helps with headaches … that come to the eyes, and should not be done after evacuating the whole body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this bleeding is in the place of the headache, and should not be done by those of a cold complexion, or who have catarrh, because it does them great harm;Car s’il li est aprés le sangle, ou sur la coste sus li sangle, ou deduit par la coste sus li sangle, et que l’on le tienne si fort qu’il ne se mueve, et que il vienne de lor chief sang, et qu’il soit au costé sus
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason, the elderly should not use it, nor those who have serious diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often heal from it become oblate, and because of this, the cupping glasses should be placed a little lower down due to the risk of oblateness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The wind-gazing in the neck is in line with the pulse of the head and the basilic, and for this reason it helps with tightness in the feet, and with splits in the gullet of the lung, and with constipation and bloating;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and one should not push it too hard, because if it is pressed too tightly, it harms the stomach and the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The wind-gazing at the two sides of the neck helps with headaches, and eye pain and inflammation, and with strangulation, and with toothache, and is in line with the pulse of the basilic;
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and you should instruct the patient to express his hand when placing it, so that he does not constrict the artery and cause a rush of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The ventilators below the chin are good for mouth diseases, and gum decay, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and they are in place of bleeding from the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilation of the armpits is good for a disease that comes from heat and fullness.
