Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The ventilators on the sides are as good as three veins in the arm, because they draw blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the bleeding person not to pierce too deeply, because the place is bare of flesh, and has veins and arteries underneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The cupping glass that is on the buttocks is good for hemorrhoids and illnesses underneath, and it should be large, and made of copper, so that it draws well;
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and by chance, if it were delicate, it would break;
et i fai grans plaies.	and it makes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The cupping glasses on the legs bleed very openly, because they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains in the loins, and in the hips, and in the bladder, and restore the flow of urine;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and are in place of two sutures, and of two ankles, and yet they weaken the body after long use, and cause paralysis in many ways.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The method of applying the cupping glass is to first place it empty, and suck gently, and apply it firmly, and move it evenly, and not stop doing this until you see the area red and swollen, and the redness of blood appearing;
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	then heat it, and re-apply the cupping glasses, and take care in the disposition of the body, for there are some with such thin skin and clear pores;
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	one should only pierce once, and one should make wide wounds, and not too deep;
et suce legierement.	and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the vein is thick, one should pierce twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to open the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very thick, then it must be struck a third time.
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to draw out a little blood, we only need to strike once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want a lot of blood, then we start again often;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the blood is thick, then pierce it deeply, and the ends should be such that the skin is pierced suddenly, and it suits someone who has tough and hard skin, and who have narrow pores, that you grease the places of the ventouses with astringent and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in the head, use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in the liver, use watercress oil, or lily, or chamomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or of balsam, or of fennel, and similar oils.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if one is being bled from tender skin and large pores, then no oil should be used, but it should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or pumpkin water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture should get up from garlic, or myrrh water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large surpluses should drink old wine, or dry water, or a decoction of aniseed or chamomile, or similar;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and it is not good to bleed with cupping glasses before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for one or two hours;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and he should not sleep after cupping, and it is good that he warms himself, both when he should be bled and when he is bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware if the person bleeding is choleric, and if the blood is too thin and inflammed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if he should eat cool things like pomegranates and endives and lettuce with garlic, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eat pulses, and meat from a pot, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those with a cold complexion should eat honey syrup, and moderate old and new wine, and pulses, and small birds and peewits;and those with a hot temperament should not eat too many pulses or meat, but rather drink cool water.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day he is bled, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some people theriac or musk before or after bleeding to strengthen the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	dilute the wine, but those who are hot-tempered should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The leeches that are used without causing pain are those placed on the liver, and the mumps, and podagra, and on the belly, and the groin, and the hips, for these members cannot be bled without pain, except to attract blood from one member to another, as we do when placing leeches on the breasts when the nipples are healthy;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to remove the viscousness that is in a member, as we do by placing leeches on the belly and groin to reduce the size of the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and removes pain when there is obstruction or stone, and it removes by its attractive power the obstruction, or the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and so it does when placed over the liver and over the stomach when there is retained flatulence; these cupping glasses are administered empty in order to suck only slightly.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water, as in the case of diseases of the pleura; in such a way one fills the cupping glass with warm water, or water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cupping glass administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it should be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and on the side near the middle it has a small hole, just big enough to push through an awl, and it should be made of copper, smooth in front so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and he has in the middle a bent rod of iron or steel, to hold a candle, and there are both large and small ones depending on the illnesses and age of those who use them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	because children's cupping glasses are different from adults', and for thin people they are different from fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should thus place this cupping glass on the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take the candle of wax or linen and put it inside the cupping glass through the rod which is inside the cupping glass, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping glass and does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the member, and one's fingers must be on the hole that we have mentioned, so that when one wants to, one can release the vapor and remove the cupping glass;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and they take the linen as before, and repeat it often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping glass therefore which is administered for pleurisy, in all acute diseases, there is no tube or aperture, and it is not removed until it is full of water, and is placed on the limb alone;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Leeches are not removed until in members where one cannot place cupping glasses because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bare flesh, such as elbow or knee, and other similar places;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of its use is such that when you find leeches in clear, clean water without mud, you should take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in fresh water for as long as they are famished, and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then cleanse the vein and apply cupping glasses, then rub the limb until it is red, and place the leeches upon it;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are flat, and itching, if it is in a place where one can apply a cupping glass, one should, because it helps a lot.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then raise the area with a bandage, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it out;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the bites heal too slowly after the body of the leech, then soak a linen cloth in cold water and place it on top until the leech is stretched out;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the bites are numerous, then place ground vitriol, or gall, and similar things on top until they are stretched out;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you can place half-peeled peas on the area and leave them until they warm up the area, and it will stop right away;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, then take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the leeches will not attach, then rub the area with fresh blood, or pierce the skin with a needle until blood comes out, and then apply the leeches; as soon as they smell the blood, they will attach.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are sucking, then powder over a little aloe and powdered glass, or ash, and they will stop immediately.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine and is a cure for fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that the fools mock this chapter, which they have never seen in any ancient book or letter;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason knowledge is strange in our land, for I have never found any good ones;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing of it except through the science of ancient books, from which I have studied so much that I have attained knowledge, and through experiment and the habit of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described in this chapter what is contained within, and abbreviated it at the end, and clearly demonstrated the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I have done in the two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we must say in the prologue of this book the subjects of the discussion and the chapters in which the sage sets his understanding, and dwells on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture, dislocation, twisting, or break occurs in someone, you must hurry to heal the patient on both sides, if anything does not heal him completely, as with weakness of the body, or old age, or frailty;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the weather is not very warm, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and eat cold foods, that is, cold joints, and bird and squirrel meat, and do not drink any wine, nor eat any fatty foods, and do not fill yourself too much with meat that fills the veins with blood, until you have reason to suspect a hot abscess or inflammation in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the patient returns to his former way of life.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, one must feed the patient foods that promote swelling and stickiness, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, eggs, and offal, and fresh fish, and wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with this swelling the bones will close up and heal more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And you should know that broken bones in the elderly and the very young cannot heal well or unite naturally due to the dryness of their limbs.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but nevertheless, reset the broken bone by pulling on the large tendons that stretch and join the limb together, as tightly as it was before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not cut off all blood flow to the area; for that reason, one should feed on rich foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you should know that there are various types of fractures in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of fracturing.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another in grinding, as with the tip of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break all over a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each part has its own function and its own unique healing process, according to what is remembered about it.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And a broken bone is apparent by its crookedness and can be identified by pressing on it with the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting or tenderness, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but there may be twisting, or splitting, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move it by hand, but rather apply the remedies that follow, and then hold it firmly in place.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And you should know that the fracture that goes into the bone, and the two parts are separated, they must now be put back together equally, as with abscesses.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if hot abscesses come, he leaves them for a day or two, until the abscesses are calm;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then he puts it back in place as easily and gently as possible, and you should know that the restoration of this one is easier than the restoration of the one with pieces;
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then they are restrained, as appropriate afterwards.Et saiches qu’il convien que tu fasses la mesme chose en celi ou il ait pieces et non pas en
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there are broken pieces of bone, they are separated into two parts, whether it is a hand or foot, or a small limb, or two tendons, or one tendon and a hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, then by all means bring the additions back into their places as you can, and be careful that your work does not cause the patient injury or pain.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust the two heads of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it with your hand if you think it is not right:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	and stretch it gently, without pulling too hard or pressing as those do who bring about a hot abscess and contraction in the limb through their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is healed, then instruct the patient to be careful not to move it, whether waking or sleeping, turning over or in any other way:
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and make sure that the limb is secure so that he does not feel any pain.Et s’il ot aprés doulour, si le ramene a son leu selonc ke tu sai, et f
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, then it is not at all, and one must put him in such a position that he feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and be careful that it is set straight, so that no crookedness comes to it when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the qualities of the broken member are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members vary in smallness and greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small members, like arms and fingers and their likes:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	and one must wrap them in soft, fine linen;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, like thigh and leg:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and one must wrap them in a wide, hard bandage, for the wide bandage envelops the entire large member and holds it tightly from all sides evenly so that there is no swelling.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then tie around it with light bandages, three or four according to the member, and press your hand tightly against all the bandage, then go above the dislocation and loosen it less so that the dislocation is pushed out a little;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the bond little by little, until you grasp a large part of the healthy tissue, then take hold of another bond, and twist back and forth on the broken area;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go to the area under the break, and pull gently, not too hard or too softly, as we have said in the first hour above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then place between the bonds, cotton or linen, until they are all even, then tie it all tightly with a bandage on top; and then put your splints well placed on top if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then place something soothing for the abscess, hot, and which reduces the swelling, and leave it thus for several days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then pull gently on your splints; they should be made of half a cane split lengthwise, or from palm wood, and made in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the star that one puts on the fracture is a bit larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and also as long as it needs to be in the small or large member;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then press on the stars as you did in the first hour, then tie a string over them gently, just as you did in the first hour over the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	the tighter it is, the better, but not too tight;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and the string should be medium thickness, not too thick or thin, and made of soft flax;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	because if the strings are thick, as I have seen foolish people make their ties with strong cords, and that is a great error, for the tie cannot be even if it is too thin, and there should not be less than two fingers' width between each star.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded in the head after the stretching of his legs while healthy, then place under them linen pads or other soft cloth so that he does not get hurt.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the bone is broken, I will describe the treatment for this later.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not good to stretch all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when a member is swollen, you must not put splints on it for more than five or seven days, or longer depending on the heat of the abscess.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	And here is the manner of ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsions:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And it is that you take flour that is stored in the walls of the mill, and cook it with plenty of egg, and put this mixture, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the plaster restoring fractures in many dispositions, especially in women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another way of plaster restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions: Prenes de la cire et l’uef et confis ensembles, et quanque il soit ben confis, mets li
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take wax and eggs and cook them together, and when it is well cooked, put in 3 barberry plants and ladani and myrrh and asafetida and gum arabic, each at 10 doses;
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	myrrh and aloe, each 5 drams;
alechil VIIII З.;	aloes wood VIIII З.;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	grind them into powder and mix with egg white;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the person's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it has a good composition and quickly restores broken bones, and benefits many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another recipe for a plaster that helps with twisting injuries:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take mugwort and honey, mix them together.
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	myrrh and aloes, mix seven parts.
acaice VI З.;	aloe six parts.
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	armenian bole ten parts, and grind well, and infuse with water or wine yolk, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another way to treat dislocated joints and bones that have been displaced from their sockets, and to ease the resulting pain, and to shrink the bone, and to heal fractures: take
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	take new lamb's wool, and boil it in oil and honey, and apply it to the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing hot abscesses and removing pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way to treat broken bones: take
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	take dry fig leaves and deadnettle leaves, and grind them together, and make an ointment from it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plaster for healing bone fractures and reducing the swelling of an abscess: take new lamb's wool, moisten it in arsole and oil, and apply it to the affected area. It also helps to restore broken bones and reduce the size of an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take the root of wormwood, chamomile, violets flowers, and wheat flour, of each one part;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and crush, and cook with wine, and if the member is scalded, cook it with moist coriander water or just water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of emplastri more forceful than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of marsh mallow, and flax seed, buckthorn berries, milk thistle, and dandelions, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of each one part;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and crush, and cook with salted water, or fresh water, or wine, depending on the heat of the member and its condition.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocrates says in his book that one should not put anything on a broken member to restore it other than a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems according to Galen that one must put on the broken member, to restore, dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another method of plaster that is good for injury and pain:Pren flos de violetes, de camomille, de mallow, et de fenugrec, de ch
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take violets, chamomile, marsh mallow, and fenugreek flowers, all in equal parts; take mugwort and peeled human hair, or bird feathers, and marsh mallow, and mix them together, and crush them, and make plaster from it and use it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then he looses it a little after, and takes care that the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone moved from its place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if he does not loosen it by hand in a few days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, or restlessness or swelling, then hurry and loosen it and remove the plaster immediately;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a light cloth, and a sponge of damp sea-sponge, and dip it in water, and lift up the place until the itching stops, and the pain is eased;Et s’il ne leve pas tant qu’il fuige la fieve, si covient li ostre l’emplaustre, et le mettre ades a l’ombre et a leu fraich, tant que li dolor se paier.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the member rest an hour, then put on lamb's wool dampened in water or rose oil, and bind it up with a cloth, until you are sure there is no hot abscess;Et s’il vient aposteme a la dent, que li dent soit mise sus ainne fraiche, et li leu sea moillie en aigue, ou oile de luisant, ou oile d’amand, si covient le mettre sus dent fraiche, tant qu’elle se
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and relieve inflammation of the member, and remove pain, then start again with gentle pressure, and a little ointment, and do not squeeze as hard as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen, and you need ointment and binding, then do it again, just as you did before.Et se il n’est pas sanez, et il ne te veult bien estraindre, si covient qu’il soit osté dou membre et mis en autrui lieu, et li membre ben liien et ben reposé.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if there is nothing of what we have said in the member, do not dislocate it until 3 or 4 or 5 or 7 days.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And sometimes leave it for 20 days according to what one sees, as long as the fracture heals and the bone nears the surface.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then reduce it further than before, and increase its flesh, as I said earlier;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the area drier than necessary, know that healing cannot occur;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then immerse it in warm water every time you dislocate it, and do so every third day, and loosen the pressure a little;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	by this work then shorten the growth of the member, and gently mend what the foolish do, who restore the crooked member.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	It is evil, and if it is done timidly, I see no other outcome than weariness and doing it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various kinds of fractures:
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many types of fractures, and various shapes, and the causes are distinct.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for there are fractures that are made by the impact of a sword, and the collar bone breaks all the way to the hyoid which is under the jawbone, as with a blow or a staff;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and because of this type of fracture is called 'a sword cut'.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Or the sword cuts the bone from above without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called 'absolute';
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and the wound of these two fractures are large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a blow with a bladed weapon, or a split or from the collarbone, or from falling on stone, or from other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a broken bone piercing through to the membrane below the bone, or on top of the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that is buried in the bone as subtle as a hair, and the split is small, and therefore this fracture is called "capillary";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound is made by a stone or by falling, or by a similar object, and drives the bone below, and the site is hairy like a blacksmith when they work on kettles;
si entre li piere dedens.	if it pierces the bone inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often in those who have moist bones in their heads, like children's heads;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it happens in all types of fractures where small pieces are separated like tiles;Et quant li os se fend et est les pieces separees, adonc covient le chief d’en tirier la piece qui est dedens, ou il li sanz
et je em parlerai en son leu.	And when the bone splits and the pieces are separated, then you must pull out the piece that is inside the wound,
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we shall know all kinds of fractures through examination, and through the corruption that is upon them, and through the foulness that is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known when one has uncovered the bone and rubbed it, if the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be wary of the signs of illness, and if you see any bad signs, such as vomiting of blood, loss of consciousness, swelling, fever, eyes bulging and reddening, and other similar things in various dispositions, then it cannot heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a fearful accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the patient comes to you first, and it is winter, then you should remove the tooth before the fourteenth day that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the spring, then you should hurry to remove the tooth before the seventh day, so that the gum beneath the tooth does not become corrupted, and the accidents we have described occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the bone fracture extends to the membrane that covers the brain, then you must split the fractured part like this:Quant tu sens li os qui est brisez, tant qu’il soit moelleux et friable, tu le rendras si fort com il fu por son naturel;
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and you must grip the head of the dislocated joint and expose the bone in every way you can, and probe the wound more gently than you can, and if bleeding occurs when exposing the bone, or an abscess forms, treat it with what is appropriate, and you must fill the area with soft rags soaked in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and let the wound rest until the abscesses are calm and bleeding is stopped;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin to cut around the bone, and this is done in two ways:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one way is to cut straight across in front, and that is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another larger cut than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second way is to have many different cuts, some narrow and some wide, and they are pointed, and made of iron:
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and work gently so you do not wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and thick, you must pierce it all around so that you can apply the trepan with chisels, not deeply enough to penetrate through the skull, and there should be a rim or ring on top of the point so that it does not go through the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	And you should have several of these so that each one comes into its own place in the thickness of the bone so that you can use chisels for all the skull.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	There are three ways to make chisels:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The technique for piercing around a broken bone is to place the chisel on the bone and twist it with your hands until you feel that the bone is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then move the chisel to another spot a little further away and do this all around. Then cut into the space between the perforations with a cutting instrument, as subtly and gently as you can, as we have said, until you pull out the bone with your hand or one of the instruments you have, such as tweezers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and make sure you do not touch the brain or the eye.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone and cut it, you should resect the thickness that remains in the bone with some other instrument like a chisel, but it should be more thin and more delicate than the other chisel;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if anything of the small bones or any scales remain, remove them easily with the instrument;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then dress the wound with tenting and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other method of treatment is that which Galen describes, which is safer;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and he highly recommends it, and it is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must expose a part of the bone, at the place where the fracture is open, so that when you have exposed that part, you shall place under the head of this lens-shaped incision, from which the fracture has occurred, in order to cut it.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side only, for the wound is open on both sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then hit it gently with a small mallet all around, taking care not to damage the membrane underneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is attached to the bone, gently pull at it, for the bone can be removed without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce through to the membrane, and the bone is only cut slightly on top, and there are small pieces, then one must smooth out that roughness, and remove the scales with a sharp rasp which you should have in various sizes, in order to adapt it to each location according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Take a large rasp first, and then a finer one afterwards, and do not stop doing this until it is smooth.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	For all other hairline and subtle fractures, you should treat them according to their specific nature:
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this is not something that can be learned by one who has dedicated himself to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is open, you should wet a linen cloth with rose oil according to the size of the wound, and place it over the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	Then take another double cloth, dip it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then apply pressure as gently as you can so as not to tear the wound, then place another bandage over it, without tightening it more than necessary to hold the wound in place.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and leave it thus for a day or two, until the abscess is soothed, then loosen it, and administer remedies such as lily roots, and wheat flour, and incense powder, and aristolache, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and make a powder from these things, and apply it to the wound, and then administer other remedies without biting;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and guard against the wound becoming dirty, so that you do not leave ointment on it, nor allow pus to gather, for when pus gathers on the membrane of the brain, it will become infected and cause great harm to the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when one applies something biting to a sore, it bites from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if darkness does not come from the medicine one has applied, but because of the power it has, one must take a portion of honey and three parts of rose oil, and mix them into a paste, and apply it to the sore;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with various treatments until he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose are broken, or one part by itself, because there are two bones in it;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and that which is underneath is cartilage, and does not break, unless it is split or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should put your little finger or a hole in the nose, and place that broken part inside your index finger, and hold it in place by force, so that the nose returns to its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.Et s’il se finde ke la brisure est a l’enbas dou neis, si covient que tu le tiennes aler a bas
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is above the nail, and the fingers cannot reach the spot, then you must use the end of a thick stick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in both parts, do likewise and hurry to reset it on the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess is calm, then put a linen tent on the head of the wound, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you place another in another part, if the fracture is there;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let the tents be so big that they fill the holes of the wound.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say that one must wet the bandages with butter, and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem to me that this is good, but one must make them wet with egg white and flour;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the tent, until the bone is stiff, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes one puts in goose feathers instead of tents, and around it a soft cloth, and the fracture is held, and the patient breathes among them;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or do what you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if hot abscesses come to the nose while you are working on it, then put a poultice of rose oil or in a little diaquilon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if there is no abscess, then put on a plaster, by force, of wheat flour, and incense powder, cooked with egg white, then place gentle compresses on top, and do not bind the wound;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the fracture of the nose is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract it with appropriate instruments for this, then close the slit, and treat with healing, warming things like plasters and ointments suitable for this;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the nose, then treat it with tenting, and insert canes of lead, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the dislocation of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated below and there is no external wound, and the break is only out of place, and not broken in two, so that it curves inside, then one can easily tell.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, for you to put your index finger into the patient's mouth;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the fracture is in the left jaw, then put your index finger from your right hand, and gently insert it into the fracture, and ease it with the other hand, and apply pressure evenly.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jaw is separated by one-sixth, then you should administer an extension of one-sixth, so that it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if there is movement of the teeth, or grating, then hold them in place with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then apply cerote over the broken jaw, and over that, place a double layer of cloth;
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and place over the wound a well-made bandage, or a piece of leather of equal length and width according to the jaw, and tie it as tightly as possible, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the swelling changes, then release it for a third of the day, and then reapply pressure where it is swollen.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	And place an ointment on top, made of ground powder with egg white or sisam flour, after you have removed the bandage.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	And place a light lining on top of the ointment, and if the ointments don't work, and the condition of the patient doesn't change, leave it until he is healed.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	many times it is healed within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if hot abscesses develop, then administer what we have already said many times.Et se il a contusion sus la mandibule, si met sus cerote, et sus le cerote lainne legiere, et li estele longes; et se li estele s’aert, met ainche sus lainne legiere, si come tu oges li contusions; et adonques covient il que li disloque la mandibule a leu.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and wound together, examine to see if any pieces of bone are missing;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	so skillfully of the host are suitable instruments to this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there remains none inside, then stitch up the wound, if it is wide, and place upon it a suitable poultice to promote healing.
de la forcele	of the armpit
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The fracture is broken several times in front, towards the shoulder, and the break is according to 3 ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	either it is broken and separated into two, and there are pieces, and this is the easiest to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work is such that when the break is without a wound, you need two ministers so that one can hold the shoulder where the fracture is;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other stretches the neck towards the affected part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then put your fingers on the break evenly so that the shape is as it should be and there is no appearance or misalignment.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to stretch further, place under the shoulder a round pillow made of cloth or woolen fabric, as thick as your necessity demands;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and hold the forceps lightly, and squeeze the spear in your hand so that you make the break even as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the collarbone out of its socket because it is too deep, then the patient should lie on his back, and place a small pillow under the shoulder, and the assistants should lift the shoulder from below, so that the collarbone bone is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	Then grasp the break with your fingers, and if you find it loose, you must split it open;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and gently pull out the pieces, and if the bone cannot join because of an overhang, then cut it with one of your knives;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but you must place under the forceps this instrument to protect the nerve:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it should be like a spoon, and not jagged, and as wide as is necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the action;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it has two heads, as you can see, and one is wide and the other narrow, according to the shape of the wound that you made when you pulled out the bone;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are certain of a hot abscess, cut open the wound, and if the rupture is small, or if you doubt it is a hot abscess, then apply the wound with bandages and dressings according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses come, soak a bandage in rose oil, garlic, and wine, and place it over the wound:
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The dislocation of the bone, when there is no wound or incision, is to place upon the bone the plaster made from mill-dust and egg white, and place light dressings on top, and if necessary, put a splint beneath the joint.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very large bandage, one palm wide, then place double draping over the dressings and plaster;
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a thin rod three digits wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the end of the bandage hangs down;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and place the rod over the fracture, and wrap the bandage around the neck, and under the healthy joint, and under the affected joint;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and realign each part, and when you see that the dislocation is aligned correctly, and you see clearly that the bone is not moving within the fracture, then release it daily, and when the ligaments loosen, restrain them.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	Have the patient lie on his back, and while he sleeps, place a small pillow under the shoulder to raise it;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	If the dislocation of the shoulder is improved by raising it, then tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless some accident happens, for up to 20 days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	Then start the poultice again if you see that it is needed, and restrain and leave him until he is healed;and then have him lie on his back, and place a small pillow under the shoulder to raise it; If the shoulder dislocation improves by raising it, then tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless some accident happens, for up to 20 days; Then start the
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored in most people within 28 days, and in less time for some.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of a shoulder dislocation
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It sometimes happens that the shoulder is dislocated or widely displaced, and it is not set right until touched;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	then, according to the pattern of the dislocation, reset it in its natural shape, in every way you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then apply powder from the mill with egg white, and light poultices, and put on top a double layer of cloth;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then place a wide and thin splint, slightly larger than the shoulder, on top, and if there is swelling beneath the splint in any part of the shoulder, apply poultices made of flax to that area so that the splint sits evenly;
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	then tie it firmly with a wide bandage so that the splint does not move from its place, and check the bandage every day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and every time it softens, he squeezes it and puts the joint back in place if it is out of position, and then the patient lies on his side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is restored within 20 or 25 days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this period is over, he releases it and is confident, for it is not an easy bone to put back in place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone has come out in front and is not under the collarbone, cut it away, and do as we have said before about heating the abscess to ease the pain.Et si li espaule est desaloiee par cause de moistor, et on la remet en son leu, et elle ne puet demorer en son leu, si revient adés et desalue par petit mouvement qui avient; si doit on la disloquer premierement, et puis la ramonyer.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The bones are sometimes broken in the middle, but that rarely happens;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it inclines downward, and the patient feels great pain and suffering, and becomes constipated and feverish, and may vomit blood, and the bones of the fracture become visible, and he feels much discomfort.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back, and he places a cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and joins the ribs with both hands, trying to put everything in order as best he can;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then he applies plasters and poultices made of subtle salt, or other light wood, and wraps it in a cloth, placing it on the broken bone so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the bandage smoothly around the back, and tighten it gently, and check every hour that the wound is healing; if it softens, then tighten it.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it needs to be loosened, because of corrosion or itching that comes up on the skin, or pain or abscess, then hurry and loosen it, and wipe off the ointment, and address whatever has come about in various ways of healing.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then reset the ointment, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the break of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that broken ribs only come from large wounds on the back, and in the chest, and only bend because they are slippery.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and feel it well with your hands as you should.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And in treatment, you must set the break evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the ointment and bind it with a bandage, if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the broken ribs are declining inward, then the patient feels great pain and piercing, just as with pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and has fainting spells, and becomes dizzy and vomits a great deal of blood, and this is a serious illness, and the ancients have placed great importance on it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that one should administer foods that swell the belly, in order to push the fracture outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make any incision unless an abscess is hot, if it has not become so already.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has become so, then we lance it to let out the pus and the unhealthy matter.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And some say that one should place cupping glasses over the area to draw out the infection, and this is sensible advice.
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	However, there is a concern that the cupping glass might attract excess fluids due to the weakness of the body.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	Some say that one should cover the affected area with warm, moist wool and place tenting between the ribs to ensure even pressure all around; then it should be treated with a poultice of pleurisy root, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear due to the bone protruding through the skin, and there is doubt about the condition, then one should cut over the area of the broken rib, and place an instrument underneath to push out the shrapnel;
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then split the bone and pull gently, and afterwards sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat it with poultices until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if a hot abscess comes, put wet bandages in rose oil, and put them on the site.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the area around the abscess as needed, and let him lie quietly on his side where he should be, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break in the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes there is a fracture of the collarbone, and it can bend;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also in the spine of the back.
