Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, then put on the plaster that we have described, then constrict it and leave it for .v. days, then loosen it and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any swelling, then wet it with warm water and rub it until it is healed.Et s’il en a une grante, si le remede est que li mains se tienne au chaud sus la grieteit, et qu’il soit eslongeit tant qu’il soit sanez; car li membres longes sont plus tost sanaiz que li courts.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on either side, sometimes at the back of the palm or the palm itself.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then pull on the finger, and push the joint back into place as far as it will go, then hold the head of the finger, and bend it towards the part that is dislocated.
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	And leave it for two days, then put it in a sling for one day.
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	And bind it up at night as we have said, and loosen it during the day, and make it move, then rebind it at night.
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And do this often until it is healed, and do the same if it is dislocated at the back of the hand, and do as before until it is healed.
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And do likewise if it is dislocated elsewhere.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	from the dislocation of the skull from the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the skull at the back or neck is dislocated, there are several dislocations, and there is no cure, for death hastens the illness.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the signs are that the bowels move without any voluntary effort, and one cannot hold it back, and often a limb becomes paralysed, in either arm or leg.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And many times there are three openings in the scrotum;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	the one that opens at the back is called "gilbositez":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	if you find that the gilbositez has come from childhood, then:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	there is no treatment or cure for it whatsoever.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancients described many ways to treat it with great detail, but there is not much benefit in all of that.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	But I have summarized it according to my understanding and created instruments in various forms.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that there is no healing or health in the gilbositeit that comes on the front toe;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which comes straight in two places, and cannot be cured other than properly cutting away the one that comes on the back, as I said;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient be stretched out on his face in one place, and have a restraint under him so that he does not hurt himself;
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then insert a firebrand into the head in the ground, and another at the feet, and tie one string under the armpits of the patient, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and two attendants hold the strings, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two firebrands;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and they are to be tied firmly, the firebrand as we have said, and the attendant puts his palms on the spine, until it straightens out.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not straighten out with this treatment, take a table three yards long, and lay it under the patient's back, and the patient should be on his side, and place the head of the table under the back, then place the middle of the table on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and place his feet on the other end of the table, pressing hard until he returns to his original position.
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if you see that it happens in the shoulder joint which turns toward the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And you should place two coals on the head of the sick person's shoulder with one arm long, and towards the feet, two others, and there should be between each coal, above and below, a palm width of space.
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	And in each coal, there should be a hole where the shoulder joint turns, and the coals should be firmly fixed in the ground so that they do not move;
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	And between each two coals, there should be a turning coal, over which the shoulder joint turns, and there should be two small coals in the turnings, each one a palm's width long, to turn the joint;
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	Then tie the string which is among the coals to the joint toward the head, and the other string toward the feet to the other joint, and each assistant turns their joint all along the string, and the master puts the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, then apply a desiccant poultice with an abundance of egg, and then the sponges, and then the cloth of a tablet three fingers wide, which covers the area of the hunchback and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a bandage, as we have said, and use the patient's subtle cooling treatment until he is healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	And if nothing helps to restore health, then one must administer softening and soothing medicines, with the cloth that we have mentioned earlier.
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	And sometimes a lump appears in the lower spine of the back, and one thinks it is a dislocation.
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	And it is the bone that protrudes, so one must not be presumptuous about it:
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	For perhaps it would bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Know that only dislocations occur at the hip and shoulder joints, not as in other joints.
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	and the hip joint is dislocated according to four parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	within and without, and before and behind;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	and more within than without, and less dislocated before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the recognition of its dislocation within is that when one joins the affected leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the knee of the affected leg appears more open than the healthy one, and the affected person cannot bend their knee towards the fire;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and the place that is nearest to them is swollen with a hot abscess, because the shoulder of the thigh comes near it.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes in defense, it is that these accidents are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of which occurs at the front, are that their leg is well according to its completion;
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	Nevertheless, do not bend the knee without pain, and if one wishes to make it walk, it cannot move forward, and it holds back its urine, and the ankle swells, and when it walks, it drags its foot.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who happens behind, it is that he cannot extend his knee, nor double it, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the veins are softened, and the head of the thigh is at the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The cause of this kind of dislocation is that you must first examine whether the dislocation is recent or old and remaining in its original position; if there is no treatment,
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	then one should not be careless.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in those with a recent dislocation, which is one of the four types of dislocations, you should quickly put the joint back into place, and push it inside and out, and move it to the right and left;
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	perhaps it will return to its place without needing further treatment.Or si tu voels que li dislocations soit aler a la fin, si covient que li dislocation soit fresche
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, you should prepare a strong bandage and extend the leg strongly with two hands, or tie it to the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	and another minister extends his hand above it in such a way that he squeezes his hands under his armpits, then tightens a cord around the thigh;
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another ties the head with a string;
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they stretch him upwards and downwards all at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension applies to all four appearances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If not, then you must put a bandage on his head.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is in the shoulder, you must support the patient on his healthy side, then place the band around the root of the thigh, and around the area under the armpit; then tighten the band above the armpit, towards the arm pit, and towards the armpit;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	then have another minister hold his arms, and embrace the thick part of the dislocated thigh, and stretch it forcefully:
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	then return to its place now;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this type of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot reset it in the manner we have described, then you should tie the patient's two feet together with a strong silk cord above the heels, and above the knees, and the affected leg should be extended two fingers more than the other;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	then let him be hung from the end of a pole, with his arms outstretched for a long time;
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	then instruct an assistant to grab the top of the thigh, and have another assistant suspend with the patient, holding the thigh firmly, for the joint will return quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is reset, then have the patient lie down as we have said for those with gout, and tighten the ligature on the affected leg properly, and on the foot as well;
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then put two coals, one on the head and one at the feet, then place the coal between the buttocks of the patient in the wound.
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and have wet cloths placed around it so that the patient does not feel the heat, then extend each limb towards him, and the helper holds the dislocated joint in his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns to its place, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put him on a table and press it as we have said in the case of dislocation, and lay the patient on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocation is in front, one should stretch the leg of the patient slowly, and according to what I have said;
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and the helper puts his weight on the sore joint, then presses with the other hand, and they stretch it down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is on the outside, one should not stretch it down or lift it up, but it must be as though the hip were dislocated to the outside, as we have said about lying on two hips.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and let it be on his face, and the bandage extended as we have said before, and one should press upon the joint at the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and it will be straight when the patient extends his legs, and they will be even;
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	then adjust the thighs, and apply the ointment, and restrain it with a bandage so that the hip does not move;
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	and let him rest for 3 or 4 days, then release it, and apply the ointment again;
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	and if you see that they are even, then restrain it as before, and let him be for 3 days;
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	then release it, and make him walk comfortably until the limb is restored.
de la dislocation dou genoil	On dislocation of the knee:
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The knee is dislocated in 3 ways:La prima, quant le capet del la cuisse entre en l’estremeite del gen
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	The first, when the head of the thigh enters into the extreme part of the knee, that is to say, within and without, and behind;La seconde, quant il est
et ne desalue point devant.	and do not dislodge it beforehand.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the sign is that you command the patient to bend his leg at the thigh, and if it does not straighten at the thigh, know that it is dislocated;
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all [dislocations] is that you make the patient sit up straight, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back to his face, and put his foot on your feet;
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	then take his knee in your palms, and pull apart with your fingers, then bend the two sides of the knee joint;
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	and another assistant extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he straightens his leg at the thigh easily;
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	and put the plaster on, and straighten the leg at the thigh, and bind them together tightly for three or four days, then loosen it;
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and do not have the patient exert themselves until their limbs are conforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the member is not at all, then administer a very strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	Heels are sometimes smashed, and sometimes completely dislocated, both internally and externally.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and tender in front at the place where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	the movements are light, and one should slightly extend the wrist in their hands when it is only sprained.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated from all sides, one must have the patient sit upright, and hold the leg straight by the ankle, above the ankle:
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left twice, then extend it upwards, and push the foot upwards firmly;
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling on the foot;
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	if it goes back into place, that is good;si elle ne veut revenir, tu le faices aler de
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	if it does not go back into place, have the patient walk around a bit, then try again, for it will go back into place;si elle ne veut revenir, tu prends
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if he cannot return in this way, then make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and firmly drive a stake into the ground between his buttocks, and wind cloth around it, so that he does not slip away.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then have one assistant hold the thigh, and another stretch out the leg with his hand or with a cord, tying it around the neck of the foot.
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then each assistant stretches him equally, and the stake is driven in between the patient's buttocks to hold him when he is stretched.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	then put your hands on the dislocation and have one assistant hold the healthy leg, and the dislocation will return easily.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is in place, put the plaster and bandages on tightly, and hold the foot firmly to the leg, being careful not to press too hard on the nerves behind the ankle.
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	then let it rest for two or three days, and if the ligature softens, then tighten it.
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	then untie it on the third or fourth day, and let the patient go about their business for four days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he goes before that time, it is not certain that he will not relapse.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a deep abscess forms, you must calm it down as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of the armpit
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the arms are dislocated, they should be stretched without force, and that is a minor matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in the lower back or foot, you should have the patient lie flat on his back or on a table, completely straight, and place your foot on the affected area, then press firmly with your foot until it pops back into place;
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	and when it is even and nothing sticks out, place a two-legged table under the foot, then tighten it firmly, and let it rest for three days, then untie it.
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let him rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound occurs with a dislocation, and one wishes to restore it, many times the patient dies.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	If you are not presumptuous in the treatment, if you are not wise in the art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and slow to anger, do not dare to proceed.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	And at the beginning of things, apply a hot poultice to an abscess, and leave the patient in God's hand if you see no hope of recovery.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when you see hope, reset the dislocated joint immediately so that the hot abscess can heal.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And when the joint is reset, apply hot poultices to soothe the abscess and treat the wound with drying ointments as appropriate.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	And if there is a fracture and small broken bones, set the bones and follow what we have said for simple fractures:Quant li membres est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	And beware of entering the path of fear, according to what I have said, for it will benefit you according to your creator, and for the safety of your weapons and your body.
